PREFACE

The curriculum and curricular materials have been developed and revised on
a regular basis with the aim of making the education objective-oriented,
practical, relevant and job oriented. It is necessary to instill the feelings of
nationalism, national integrity and democratic spirit in the students and equip
them with morality, discipline and self reliance, creativity and
thoughtfulness. It is essential to develop in them the linguistic and
mathematical skills, knowledge of science, information and communication
technology, environment, health and population and life skills. It is also
ni ry to bring in them the feeling of preserving and promoting arts and
aesthetics, humanistic norms, values and ideals. It has become the need of
the present time to make the students aware of respect for ethnicity, gender,
disabilities, languages, religion, cultures, regional diversity, human rights
and social values so as to make them capable of playing the role of
responsible citizens. This textbook has been developed in line with the
Secondary Level Science Curriculum, 2071 by incorporating the
recommendations of various education commissions and the feedback
obtained from various schools, workshops, seminars and interaction
programs attended by the teachers, students and parents.

 

 

   

  

In bringing out the textbook in this form, the contribution of the
Executive Director of the Curriculum Development Centre (CDC) Krishna
Prasad Kapri, Dr. Hridhaya Ratna Bajracharya, Umanath Lamsal, Baburam
Gautam, Pramila Bakhati, Puspa Raj Dhakal, Devraj Gurung, Keshar Khulal,
Manumaya Bhattrai. The content of the book was edited by Yubraj Adhikari.
Language of the book was edited by Ramesh Prasa Ghimire. The layout and
artworks of the book were done by Jayaram Kuikel. CDC extends sincere
thanks to all those who have contributed in developing this textbook.

This textbook contains a variety of learning materials and exercises which
will help learners to achieve the competency and learning outcomes set in
the curriculum. Each unit contains various interesting activities and the
content required for meaningful learner engagement and interaction. There is
uniformity in the presentation of the activities which will certainly make it
convenient for the students. The teachers, students and other stakeholders are
expected to make constructive comments and suggestions to make it a more
useful learning material.

cna Force

We are familiar with several interesting facts related to our daily life like:
when an object is allowed to fall freely from certain height, it is always
attracted toward the surface of the earth. Similarly, a stone thrown sideways
moves in the curve path and ultimately falls towards the earth’s surface.
Likewise, in the solar system, the moon revolves around the Earth and the
Earth revolves round the sun in their orbits. It seems simple to us. But we
can’t analyze it in all the cases. To get the answer of such questions discuss in
group and go through the following topics.

Gravitation

Before sixteenth century, it was believed that the earth was at the centre of the
universe around which planets and the sun revolve round it. This model was
assumed as geocentric model. Onward, Nicholas Copernicus introduced a
heliocentric model which assumed that the sun lies at the centre and all the
planets revolve round it in their fixed orbit. In seventeenth century, observing
through a telescope, Galileo found that there were four satellites revolving
round the Jupiter. Hence, Newton tried to find out the reason why these
planets revolve round the sun and he began to investigate on it. During this
observation he propounded the famous law of gravitation in 1687 A.D. by
which the force of gravitation between two

bodies could be measured. *

According to Newton, the bodies in the universe
attract each another. This force of attraction is
called force of gravitation. For example, the Moon»
earth attracts the moon and the moon attracts the
earth too. Similarly, the earth attracts the Jupiter
and the Jupiter attracts the Earth.

The effect of force of attraction of a big body on Moon ott

a small body can be observed but that of a small

body on a big one cannot be observed. The sun is so large that even the sum
of the masses of all its planets and the satellites is only about 0.0015" part of
mass of the sun. Due to the gravitational force between the sun and the earth,
the earth keeps on moving around the sun. Similarly, the gravitational force
between the satellites and planet makes the satellites to revolve round the
planets. Thus, the gravitational force is responsible for the existence of the
solar system.

  

Science- 10 1


The effect of gravitation can be experienced more on liquid than solid. Hence,
we see tides in the sea and ocean due to the force of gravitation of the moon
and the sun on the earth when they lie on the same straight line.

Newton's Universal Law of Gravitation

There is a force of attraction between everybody in the universe. That force is
called force of gravitation. Newton's law of gravitation states that "The force
of gravitation between any two bodies is directly proportional to the product
of their masses and inversely proportional to the square of the distance
between their centers."

Let us consider, two bodies A and B having masses m; and mp respectively
are separated by a distance 'd'. If the force of attraction between them is F,
then according to the law of gravitation,

In this case, G is defined as the force of gravitation which exists between two
bodies of unit masses separated by a unit distance. Its value remains the same
throughout the universe and is independent of the nature and size of the
bodies as well as the medium between them. Since the law of gravitation can
be applied to each and every objects in the universe irrespective of their
masses, sizes, medium and the distance between them, it is also known as the
universal law of gravitation.

To know the relation among the force of gravitation, mass and distance in
various circumstances, let’s study the following conditions.

Gravity

We all know that the earth seems to be spherical
in shape. It may be surprising to think how
people can stay on such spherical shaped earth. A
person living in Nepal will have his head faced
toward the sky while standing on the around
whereas a person standing in the USA, just
opposite to Nepal, will too have his head faced
toward the sky while doing so. The reason
behind it is that the earth pulls both of them o& fig. 14
towards its center with a force known as the force of gravity of the earth.
Even while we walk, run, jump and stand, the force of attraction of the earth
affects us. This force also affects on the construction of house, road, bridge,
etc,

Gravity of the earth is the force of attraction of the earth on the objects within
its gravitational field. Thus, the force by which a planet /heavenly body pulls
every object towards its centre is called its gravity.

 

All planets and satellites have their own gravity but the magnitude of force of
gravity depends upon mass and radius. It increases with increase in the mass
of the body. Also it decreases with increase in radius of the body. For
example, mass of Jupiter is 319 times more than that of the earth but its
gravity does not increase highly in comparison to its mass. Its gravity is
reduced by radius. Thus, the gravity of the Jupiter is only 2.5 times than that

Science- 10 6


of the earth, Since weight is the force of gravity experienced by an object, it
can be calculated on the basis of Newton's Universal law of gravitation.

The force of gravity of a planet acting on a body is the weight of that object
on that planet.

planet and G = gravitational constant

 

 

 

 

Here, the radius of the planet is taken as the approximate distance between the
planet and the object because the object lies on its surface.

All planets and heavenly bodies have their own gravity. The body having
more mass has more gravity. Thus, the earth has more gravity than the moon.
The gravity of a heavenly body acting on a body with more mass (is more)
than that on a body with less mass (wam keeping g constant). Therefore, it is
difficult to lift a larger stone than a smaller stone. It is observed that, the
gravity of the moon is only 1/6 of the earth. Thus, any object weighing 600N
on the earth only weighs 100N on the surface of the moon.

Acceleration due to gravity

It is studied in junior classes that acceleration is developed on a moving body
when external force is applied in the direction of motion. Likewise,
acceleration is developed on every falling object due to gravity.

‘The acceleration produced in a freely falling body due to the force of gravity
of a planet is called acceleration due to gravity.

It is denoted by symbol 'g' and its SI unit is meter / second? (m/s’). The
acceleration due to gravity of all freely falling objects will be the same. In this
context, an Italian scientist Galileo conducted an experiment in 1590 A.D. As
Galileo dropped small and large objects simultaneously from the top of the
leaning tower of Pisa, both the objects reached the ground at the same time.
This proved that both the objects attained equal magnitude of acceleration due
to gravity.

Science- 10 8


Activity 1.1
Take two stones with different size but having about equal density. Drop both
of them from a height at the same time. Place a metal or a tin plate on the
surface where the stones strike. Listen carefully to the sound produced when
stones strike on the plate.

Again, make a ball out of a paper sheet. Take another unfolded paper sheet.
Drop both of them at the same time. And discuss on following questions.

1, Will the small and large stones hit the ground at the same time?
Why?

2. Will both sheets of paper, one made into a ball and another unfolded,
reach the ground at the same time?

3. What conclusion can be drawn from it?
Feather and Coin experiment

Take about a 1m long glass tube as shown in the figure. Put a coin and a
feather at one end and close it with a cap. Then turn it upside down. It will be
observed that the coin drops faster than the feather. Then, take the air out of
the tube and repeat the same experiment. You will see that the coin and the
feather falling simultancously. It happens so because the acceleration due to
gravity is same in all objects irrespective of their masses.

Let us link the above conclusion with the activity 1.1. In case of dropping
small and large pieces of stones, both of
them hit the ground at the same time. The TT

no air. The resistance due to air increases

Acceleration due to gravity of earth

It has already been made clear that the acceleration due to gravity on the earth
is inversely proportional to the square of radius of the earth. As the earth is
not a perfect sphere, the radius(R) of the earth at the poles is minimum. Thus,
the value of acceleration due to gravity (g) is maximum (9.83 m/s’) at the
poles. Likewise, the radius (R) at the equator is maximum, so the value of
acceleration due to gravity (g) is minimum (9.78 m/s”). However, the average
value of ‘g’ on the earth’s surface is assumed as 9.8m/s”.

Now, let’s find the acceleration due to gravity of the earth of mass 6 x 107
kg and radius 6380 km. We have,

Mass and weight
Mass

The total quantity of matter contained in a body is called its mass. It is related
to the inertia of an object i.e. larger the mass greater is the inertia and vice
versa, The mass of a body remains the same wherever in the earth or in the
every part of the universe, Therefore mass of a body always remains constant.
It is measured with a physical balance or a beam balance. The mass of a body
cannot be zero. It’s S.I unit is kilogram (kg). Mass is a scalar quantity.

Mass of an object depends on total number of atoms (particles) and average
mass of atom.

Weight

Weight of a body is the force of gravity acting on that body. Thus, the weight
of a body is defined as the force with which it is pulled towards the centre of
the earth or a planet. It is measured by a spring balance and its S.I. unit is
Newton (N). The weight of a body at a place depends on

Science- 10 12


«mass of the body (m).
+ the value of acceleration due to gravity at the place (g).

The weight of a body is the product of its mass and acceleration due to
gravity. Acceleration due to gravity varies from place to place. That’s why the
weight of a body also varies. For example, radius of the carth is shorter in
polar region than at equator, so the value of g is more at poles. As a result,
weight of an object becomes more at the poles than that at the equator.

Also, weight of an object in Terai is more than that at the top of a mountain.
The weight of an object decreases with the increase in the distance from the
centre of the earth.

Freefall

Ifa sheet of paper and a piece of stone are dropped from certain height on the
earth's surface simultaneously, which one will strike on the surface at first?
Why is there difference in time of fall? Obviously, the piece of stone will hit
the ground before the sheet of paper touches the surface. In such case, the
sheet of paper experiences more air resistance than the piece of stone. The air
resistance lowers the velocity of sheet of paper. But if we drop both paper and
stone in vacuum, they will reach to the surface simultaneously. The
acceleration produced on them is equal despite their unequal mass. So, they
are freely falling objects.

Tn fact, the fall of a body under the effect of gravity in the absence of external
resistance is called freefall.

The acceleration produced on an object during the free fall is equal to the
acceleration due to gravity at the place.

The surface of the moon is not covered by the air. So, the best example of free
fall could be a body falling towards the surface of the moon. Furthermore,
when astronauts drop hammer and a feather on the moon’s surface, they fall
together. Both of them are said to be in freefall.

Weightlessness

Weight of a body on the earth is the force with

which the earth attracts it, We measure the

weight by standing on a weighing machine. we ceening the ere
Suppose a weighing machine is placed on the fig. 1.4

floor of a “lift” parked at the top floor of a tall building, and a man is standing
on the weighing machine. The weighing machine will show the weight of the
man on its scale. Now, if the lift is allowed to fall freely, then both, the
weighing machine as well as the man standing on it, would fall downward
with the same acceleration (g). Under this condition of free fall, it is not
possible for the man to exert weight on the machine because the earth pulls
the weighing machine as rapid as the man, So when the lift is falling freely
under the action of gravity; the weighing machine placed in it would show
zero weight for the man standing on it. And we say that the man is weightless
in a freely falling lift. From the discussion, we conclude that an object is said
to be ‘weightless’ when it is falling freely under the action of gravity.

The effect of weightlessness can be shown by using a spring balance with a
piece of stone hanging on its hook. When the spring balance with hanging
stone is held by hand, it shows the weight of stone as shown in figure 1.5 (a).
Now, release the spring balance; along with its hanging stone and read the
weight of stone as it falls down. It will be observed that when the spring
balance and the stone are falling freely, the spring balance shows zero weight
for the stone as shown in figure 1.5 (b). So, under the conditions of free fall,
the stone is said to be experiencing “weightlessness”.

held by the hand, it shows a certain freely along with stone, it shows a zero reading
weight (Here the weight is 500 grams) the stone is in the condition of ‘weightless’.

Activity
Take a plastic sheet and cut it out into a circular shape with radius about
15cm. Make small holes near the edge of the circle at about equal distance.
Tie a thread at each hole in such a way that the lengths of the threads are
equal. Make it into a parachute by tying an object at the ends of the threads
and observe its falling velocity after dropping it from certain height.

Summary

1, The gravitational force developed between any two objects is directly
proportional to the product of their masses and inversely proportional to
the square of the distance between their centers.

2. The gravity of the earth is the force with which it attracts an object
towards its centre. Others planets or satellites also have their own gravity.

3. The acceleration produced in a freely falling body is called the
acceleration due to gravity.

4. The attraction due to gravity developed in a freely falling body is
independent of its mass.

5. The acceleration due to gravity of an object falling on the earth is
inversely proportional to the square of the radius of the earth.

The force of gravity acting on a body is called its weight.

7. Free fall is defined as the fall of an object under the effect of gravity only
without any resistance.

8. There is no perfect freefall on the earth due to air resistance.

Science- 10 15


9. An object feels weightlessness as a result of free fall.

10. Weightlessness is the condition in which the effective weight of a body
becomes zero due to the zero reaction force of the earth or other heavenly
bodies.

Unit 2

Have you ever thought how a normal human (driver) can run or stop heavy
vehicles like truck, bus etc? How do huge ships along with a large number of
people float on the sea? A driver can stop heavy vehicles on applying very
less amount of force because the brakes of these vehicles work on the basis of
hydraulic press, And the working principle of ship is based on law of
floatation. In this chapter, we study about these principles and other
concerned topics in detail.

Pascal's Law

Blaisé Pascal, born in 1623 AD, is a French mathematician, physicist,
inventor and writer. He propounded the law of liquid pressure (Pascal’s law)
which states that “the pressure exerted at any point in an enclosed liquid, is
transmitted equally in all direction throughout the liquid”.

Activity 2.1

To demonstrate that liquid transmits pressure equal
in all direction, take a plastic bag and fill it with
water and tie its month. Make lots of small holes on
it with the help of a pin. Press the plastic bag gently,
water comes out from all holes simultaneously as
shown in figure 2.1.

'P’, Ultimately, same magnitude of pressure is transmitted
in all three pistons B, C and D which can be noticed by
the equal displacement of all three pistons due to
pressure.

 

 

Pascal's law is applied in the construction of hydraulic
machine such as hydraulic lift, hydraulic press, hydraulic Fig. 2.2
brakes, etc.

Density of Liquid and Upthrust

It is a matter of common experience that a body appears lighter when it is
immersed in water. While drawing a bucket full of water from well, we feel
lighter when it is inside the water and suddenly it becomes heavier when it
comes out of water. Inside the water, bucket experiences the upward force of
water. The net upward force exerted by a liquid on a body which is
completely or partially immersed in it is called up thrust or buoyant force.

If w; and w3 are weight of a body in air and water respectively, the upthrust of
the water is given by U = wi-w9. It means the body appears lighter when it is
immersed in a liquid than in air due to upthrust of liquid.

Upthrust experienced by a body depends upon the volume of its immersed
part and density of liquid. Larger the volume of immersed body greater is the
up thrust. Similarly up thrust is directly proportional to the density of liquid.
So, greater the density of liquid, greater will be the upthrust.

water is greater than that of fresh water, which results greater upthrust in salty

Archimedes’ Principle

 

Archimedes was born in 287 BC in Syracuse,
Sicily. He was a mathematician, physicist,
engineer, inventor and astronomer too. After
performing many experiments on upthrust,
Archimedes finally formulated Archimedes’
principle which states “when a body is immersed partially or completely in a
liquid (fluid), it experiences an upthrust which is equal to the weight of liquid
(or fluid) displaced”

Upthrust = Weight of displaced liquid Spring balance

Do you know?
Archimedes principle is
also applicable to gases.

Law of floatation

The law of floatation states “when a body floats in a liquid it displaces the
liquid whose weight is equal to its own weight”.

For a floating body,

Weight of floating body = weight of displaced liquid.

Atmospheric pressure
Our earth is surrounded by a layer of air called atmosphere. The gases in the
atmosphere are nitrogen, oxygen, carbon dioxide and other gases. The
atmosphere has a mass of about 5.15 x 10'* kg and extends up to about
1000km from the surface of the earth, So, it exerts pressure on the surface of

the earth, The pressure exerted by the weight of air on the surface of the earth
is called atmospheric pressure. It is also called barometric pressure.

At sea level, the atmospheric pressure is about 1.01 x 10°pascal or 760mm of
Hg. It is also known as one standard atmosphere pressure. The atmospheric
pressure varies from place to place on the surface of the earth as the density of
air in the atmosphere decreases with altitude and thickness of the atmosphere.

Atmospheric pressure has effects on all the objects and living organism. Both
low and high atmospheric pressure is unsuitable for living organism.

Activity 2.6

Fill a glass with water upto the rim and cover it with a postcard or thick piece
of paper. Press gently with palm to remove any air bubbles present. Then
gently hold the glass and make it upside down putting one palm over the
postcard, slowly remove the palm. The postcard remains attached with the
water surface and the water in glass does not fall. This is because upward
force on the postcard i.e. atmospheric pressure is greater than the downward
force on the postcard due to weight of the water.

Science- 10 25


Measurement of atmospheric pressure

The atmospheric pressure can be measured with the help of a device called

barometer. This scientific instrument was invented by

the scientist named

Evangelist Torricelli in 1643. There are different types of barometer such as
mercury barometer, aneroid barometer etc. But in this unit, we will discuss

about mercury barometer only.
Mercury barometer

‘A mercury barometer consists of a glass tube of 100 cm
in length. At first, it is filled completely with mercury
and then it is inverted over mercury filled trough as
shown in figure. There should not be air bubbles inside
the tube. Therefore special attention and precautions are
taken to avoid the air bubbles inside the glass tube.
While doing so the mercury level in the glass tube falls
slightly creating a vacuum at the top as shown in figure.
This vacuum so created is called toricellian vacuum,
The tube is made erect with the help of support and is
graduated with scale. When the atmospheric pressure

Some common devices that use air pressure
Syringe

Syringe is a medicinal device used in the hospitals and

clinies for injecting

medicines inside the body and to cject blood from the body of the patients.

Mainly, syringe consists of a piston, a barrel and a needle.

First of all, piston is pushed into the barrel in
order to take out air from it. Then the needle
of the syringe is inserted into the liquid
(medicine, blood etc). Since all the air of the
barrel is taken out, the pressure in the barrel
decreases. The piston of the syringe is pulled
slowly. As we pull the piston, there occurs
vacuum in the storage cylinder. As the liquid
always move from higher pressure region to

 

low pressure region, the medicine moves toward the storage cylinder as there
is low pressure. Now, the needle is taken out from the bottle and inserted in
the blood streams of the patient. As we push the piston, the medicine moves

Science- 10

26


into the body through blood vessel. Similarly, the blood is ejected out from
the body of the patients.

Air pump

The pump used to fill up the atmospheric air into
the rubber tubes of vehicles, bicycles, etc. is called
air pump. Any air pump consists of a piston, a
barrel and a rubber pipe. Piston is provided with a
valve. The piston valve opens when the piston
moves up and it gets closed when the piston is
pushed down. Rubber pipe is connected to the
rubber tube in which atmospheric air is to be
filled. This tube consists of a valve too which

controls the back flow of air. Fig. 2.11

When the piston moves down in barrel the pressure in the barrel increases, the
air in it gets squeezed. Due to which the valve in the piston is closed and the
valve in rubber tube is opened. The squeezed air moves into the rubber tube
through the rubber pipe. This is called down stroke. At the same time, the air
from the atmosphere enters into the barrel above the piston through a small
hole provided on the top of the barrel.

When piston moves up, the pressure in the barrel decreases, the valve in
rubber tube closes and the valve in the piston opens. This is called upstroke.
During this stroke, the air above the piston is collected below the piston. The
repeated action of down stroke and upstroke fills the air inside the rubber
tube.

Water pump

The manually operating pump which is
used for lifting water from well or any
underground reservoir is called water
pump. A water pump consists of a piston
with handle, a barrel, a metal pipe. The

   
    
   
  

Pump rod

piston with handle moves up and down in ‘ner
the barrel, It is provided with a piston Pion
valve which opens when piston moves _—

down and closes when piston moves up.
The pipe is fitted at the bottom of the — sxione bang ata
barrel goes to the water reservoir. Another eS
valve (foot valve) is provided at the
bottom of the barrel, which opens when

Science- 10 27


the piston moves up and it gets closed when the piston moves down.
Upstroke

Just like air pump, water pump also works in two strokes. When the piston is
moved upward with the help of the handle, the pressure in the barrel decreases
and the valve in the piston is closed. The air pressure above the surface of
water pushes the water up then the foot valve at the bottom of the barrel opens
and the water enters into the barrel. This is called upstroke.

Down stroke

When the piston moves down, the pressure in the barrel increases and the
valve in the piston is opened and foot valve gets closed. At this time, the
water collected in the barrel below the piston moves up through piston valve.
This is called down stroke. During this stroke, water comes out of barrel
collected as per necessity.

Summary

1. Pascal's law states that the pressure exerted at any point in an enclosed
liquid is transmitted equally in all direction throughout the liquid.

2. Inany hydraulic machine, following relation is valid.

ALR
AL Ag
Up thrust of any liquid is directly proportional to its density.

4. Archimedes principle states that when a body is immersed partially or
completely in a fluid, if experiences up thrust which is equal to the
weight of fluid displaced.

5. Law of floatation states that when a body floats in a liquid it displaces the
liquid whose weight is equal to its own weight.

6. Law of floatation is applied in the operating ships, submarines, hot air
balloons, etc.

7. The pressure exerted by the atmosphere due to its weight is called
atmospheric pressure.

8. Atmospheric pressure is measured by using scientific instrument
called barometer.

9. The devices such as syringe, air pump, water pump, etc. are
constructed on the basis of air pressure.

Science- 10 32


Unit 3 Energy

After a hard games or a long run, one often hears the comment:’ Oh I am
finished! I have no energy left.’ Most people feel like this at the end of the
day after having a day’s work. The energy they had in the morning has been
spent during the day. And after their meal you may hear from them” I am full
of energy again”. What does food do?

Food enables us not only to breath but also to perform the activities like
running, carrying books to school or playing a game. Just as a motor car needs
fuel to run, so do our bodies need energy which is supplied by the food. Fuel
supplies, energy to a car and makes it run. Food supplies energy to enable us
to carry out various activities.

Sources of energy

We get energy from different sources. The substances which can provide
enough useful energy at a steady rate over a long period of time is called
source of energy. There are mainly two sources of energy -non renewable
sources of energy and renewable sources of energy

Non renewable sources of energy

The sources of energy which are depleted or exhausted after a certain period
of time if they are used continuously are called non renewable sources of
energy. These sources have been accumulated in nature over long period of
time, e.g. coal, mineral oil, natural gas and other fossil fuels. They take a long
interval of time to form again when they get used up.

Renewable sources of energy

The sources of energy which are inexhaustible and can be replaced as they
have been used up are called renewable sources of energy. They can be used
again and again.

These sources are available in an unlimited amount in nature and develop
within a relatively short period of time, e.g. solar energy , wind energy, hydro
power energy, geothermal energy, tidal energy, biomass energy, etc. These
sources of energy can be replaced in short interval of time if they are
exhausted at their original place.

Science- 10 33


Sun as the ultimate source of energy

The sun plays a vital role for the existence of living things on the earth. It
provides energy to all the living organisms directly or indirectly. We use
fossil fuel, hydro electricity, bio fuel, tidal energy, geo thermal energy which
are also the direct or indirect forms of solar energy. Whatever sources of
energy are available on the earth they are transformed from the solar energy.
‘Thus, it is a fact that the sun is the ultimate source of all types of energy.

Plants prepare food by photosynthesis using solar energy. The animals obtain
their food from the plants for their survival. Thus, the energy consumed from
plants by animals is converted into their muscular energy which is also the
indirect form of solar energy. Fossil fuels are formed from these plants and
animals buried in the earth for millions of the years when they get heated in
the absence of oxygen. So, fossil fuel is also an indirect product of solar
energy.

Formation of river, ocean and rain is only possible by the evaporation of
water by the heat of the sun. The flowing water is used to rotate turbines and
generate hydroclectricity. Thus, the hydroclectricity is the outcome of solar
energy.

When the air of a place gets heated up by the heat from the sun, the hot rises
up creating a partial vacant space. The cooler air from another region moves
towards such vacant place with great speed forming wind. Hence, wind
energy is also considered as an indirect product of solar energy.

Likewise, biomass is the organic matter and residue, which is formed with the
help of solar energy. Due to the above reasons, the solar energy or the sun is
the ultimate source of energy.

Facts about the Sun

The sun is the large massive heavenly body containing hydrogen (70%) and
helium (28%).

Mass: 2 x 10°kg (3.33 <10° times greater than the Earth)
Diameter: 1.4 x 10° km (10 times greater of the Earth)
Temperature of the surface: 5700°C

Core temperature: 1.5  10’°C (approximately)

Energy radiation: 4 x 10°°J/s (approximately)

Average solar energy received by the Earth: 1.4 kW/m’ per second

Science- 10 34


Sources of energy and their uses
Fossil fuel

The remains of dead animals and plants which were buried under the earth’s
crust millions of years ago are called fossils. The fuel formed from such
fossils is called fossil fuel. Coal, minerals oils and natural gases are formed
from the fossils and hence they are fossil fuel.

The plants and animals of millions of years ago buried deep inside the earth
get converted into fossil fuel, when they get subjected to high pressure and
temperature.

Coal

Coal is used as fuel in industries, factories and trains. It is also used in metal
industries like iron, steel, etc. In Nepal, the occurrence of high quality coal,
i.e. anthracite has not yet been detected. However, low quality coal (lignite)
mines are found in Dang district. It takes millions of years for the formation
of coal. As coal is no renewable, they should be used rationally.

Mineral oil

Petrol, diesel, kerosene are called mineral oil. They are mainly used in
vehicles like motor car, ship, aeroplane, etc. These mineral oil are extracted
from the deep mines beneath the surface of the earth. Crude oil is taken out
from the mine. They vary in their carbon content, volatile matter and moisture
context, When the crude oil is refined, we get petrol, kerosene, diesel, etc.
along with residual oil. On further refining the residual oil, we get asphalt,
paraffin and lubricating oil. Asphalt is used for road construction. The raw
materials used for making plastics are also produced after refining the mineral
oil. Liquefied petrolcum gas (LPG), which is used as cooking gas is also
obtained during the purification of crude oil. It takes millions of year for the
formation of mineral oil. It is also the non renewable source of energy. The
advantages of fossils fuel are mentioned below.

i. Fossil fuels are cheaper and easily available..
ii, It can easily be transported in any needy places.

iii, It is used for various purposes like to run industries, automobiles,
generators, etc.

iv. It can also be used to generate electricity.

Science- 10 35


Hydropower

Hydro electricity generated in the hydropower station is the source of energy
which is used to run electrical appliances like computer, radio, TV, telephone,
etc. Huge amount of electricity can be generated from the current of fast
flowingwater. Although the production cost for the generation of
hydroelectricity is high in the beginning, it is cheaper on the long run.

Hydropower is the most potential source of energy in Nepal. In the world’s
list, Nepal belongs to the second richest country in hydroelectric power
potentially. It has been estimated that total hydropower capacity of Nepal is
about 83,000 MW but at present less than 1000MW of electricity is generated.

The advantages of hydroelectricity are mentioned below.

i, Although the production cost is high, hydroelectricity is cheaper in long

ii, It supplies energy without pollution.
iii, It is a renewable source of energy. So it will never get exhausted.
iv. It is easy to transform to other form of energy. Thus it is considered as a
multipurpose source of energy.
v. It is widely used in electric and electronic devices.
Alternative sources of energy

Those sources of the energy which are developed to reduce the load on non
renewable sources of energy are called alternative sources of energy. All the
renewable and perpetual sources of energy are considered as alternative
sources of energy. Such sources of energy are used to maintain the storage of
the conventional source of energy. Non renewable sources of energy exhaust

Science- 10 36


after their broadly use and causes energy crisis in near future. To solve this
crisis problem, it is necessary to use the alternative sources of energy. In the
present context of the world, following alternative sources are being used as
alternative sources of energy.

Bio mass

The agricultural residue, animal waste, food weeds, etc. are collectively called
biomass. The energy obtained from biomass is called biomass energy. Hay,
straw, stalks of jute and maize, husk, saw dust, firewood, animal dung, etc.
are the sources of biomass energy. In rural areas of Nepal, the cattledung is
changed into circular or cylindrical shape and then dried over the sun light to
use as fuel (guintha).

The biogas plant is constructed using modern technology so that the gas
produced from cattle waste in the bio gas plant is used to set fire which is free
from pollution. It contains methane, carbon dioxide, hydrogen and hydrogen
sulphate gases.

The waste product obtained after producing biogas can further be used as
organic fertilizer in agriculture. Human wastage and poultry droppings can
also be used to produce biogas. Government has also provided help and
subsidy for the construction of bio gas plant. The use of bio-fuel is effective in
village and hilly regions. Following are the advantages of biogas.

i. The raw materials cost no money and are easily available in rural
areas.

ii, Tt. can be used for cooking as well as lighting purpose.

iii, It does not produce smoke on burning and hence it does not cause air
pollution.

iv. The wastage product obtained after the production of biogas can be
used as a good organic fertilizer.

Nuclear Energy

The enormous amount of energy is released when two or more nuclei undergo
a nuclear reaction. This type of energy is called nuclear energy. Nuclear
energy can be produced either by fusing nuclei or splitting the heavy nucleus.

When two or more light nuclei combine to form heavy nucleus under high
temperature and pressure, the large amount of energy released in the form of
heat and light. This process is called nuclear fusion. Hydrogen bombs are
made on the basis of reaction involved in such process. In the sun and stars,

Science- 10 37


there is regular process of nuclear fusion reaction resulting the production of
heat and light energy continuously.

The process in which an unstable nucleus of heavy atom (like Uranium-235)
splits up into two lighter nuclei with the liberation of a large amount of energy
is called nuclear fission.

The desigentreted mass during fusion and fission reaction get converted into
energy according to the relation propounded by Albert Einstein. Einstein’s
mass energy relation is used for the calculation of nuclear energy. According
to it, mass (m) can be converted into energy (E) equivalent to me?[ E=mc’],
where c is the velocity of light in vacuum, i.e. 3 x 10%m/s.

Nuclear fission process is carried out in a nuclear power plant. The heat thus
produced is used to obtain stem from boiling water. The steam operates the
large steam engines which run

generator to produce electricity. a

Tidal energy Fig, 3.2

Nowadays, new techniques are developed to generate electricity from the
tides and the waves of ocean. The tides occur in the oceans due to the
gravitation force of the sun and the moon on the water of oceans.

The water carried by the tides can be collected in tidal dams constructed at the
certain height of seashores. During low tide, the level of ocean falls below the
level of water in the dam and then the water released to fall on the turbine
which drives the generator to produce electricity. The tidal energy can
produce electricity only at certain time and for a short period and also the
process needs suitable sites. But this source of energy is not possible in our
country.

Science- 10 38


Wind energy

Traditionally, wind energy has been used as important source of energy. It is
being used to drive windmills, which in turn operate water lifting pumps and
flour mills. It is renewable source of energy and it does not produce any
environmental pollution.

by the blowing air is called wind energy.

Geothermal energy

The inner and outer core of the earth is extremely hot. The temperature below
the earth’s surface increases by about 30°C per kilometre in non volcanic
region, whereas it increases at the rate of 80°C per kilometre in active
volcanic regions.

In order to obtain geothermal energy, two parallel holes are drilled deep
below the earth’s crust. Water is passed through a hole which gets converted
into stem due to the enormous heat hidden below the earth crust. The stem
thus formed is carried out through another hole which is used to rotate
turbines to generate electricity. So, the energy that can be obtained from the
heat present inside the earth is called geothermal energy.

Energy crisis

 

il fuels are being used as the major sources of energy till now. The
natural gas, coal and mineral oil have been fulfilling about 80% energy
demand of the world. The sources of these fuels are mines but they are
limited in nature. Also the sources of these fuels are not renewable. Therefore,
it is very likely that the storage of fuel is used up in the near future.

 

According to a survey done in 1984 AD, it was predicted that the mineral oil
reserves will have been emptied within 25 to 30 years but it has been
estimated in mid Eastern Asia that there is still new storage of oil three times
bigger than the existing one. The demand for these minerals oil and coal is
increased by 2.3% every year with the pace of development. According to
various sources, storage of these minerals oils will be depleted by 2037 AD.
Thus, the world is likely to face a problem of scarcity of energy for daily use.

 

The future scarcity of energy sources on the earth due to over population,
urbanisation and industrialization is called energy crisis.

Present status of energy use and its conservation

At present, 35% of energy demand of the world has been covered by mineral
oil. The consumption of this non renewable source of energy has been
increased with rapid population growth and various development activit
Similarly, the consumption of coal is more in the industrialized countrie
About 27% of energy demand has been covered by coal and yearly it is

 

Science- 10 40


increasing by 2.3%. Biomass energy is being used mainly in rural parts of
developing countries. It covers about 13% of the energy need of the world.
Hydro electricity is supplying about 5% of the commercial energy used in the
world whereas nuclear energy covers about 3% of energy demand. Every
individual and local level must be conscious about the energy crisis.
Following steps can be considered to save the energy.

i. Alternative sources of energy should be developed and used wisely.
ii, Non renewable sources of energy should be preserved for the future.

iii, Rapid population growth should be controlled and awareness about the
importance of energy conservation should be created in public.

Summary

1. The inexhaustible sources of energy which can be regained in the nature
in short interval of time are called renewable sources of energy.

2. The energy source that cannot be regained once it is depleted is called non
renewable energy source i.e it takes millions of year to. regenerate.

3. The ultimate source of energy in this earth is the Sun. The sources of
energy like wood, coal, mineral oil, hydropower, wind etc. are the
outcomes of solar energy.

4. Hydroelectricity is cheaper, pollution free, renewable and easy to transmit.
5. The waste materials of plants and animals are called biomass.

6. Coal and minerals oils are formed from fossils so they are called fossil
fuels.

7. The scarcity of energy that is likely to happen due to the depletion of fuel
reserves is known as energy crisis.

8. Those sources of energy which are used to reduce the load an non
renewable sources of energy are called alternative sources of energy.

9. The habit of conserving fuel should be practiced in order to solve energy
crisis.

Science- 10 43


unit 4 Heat

When we rub our palms together, palms become hot. Similarly, when we
pump air into the tires of a bicycle continuously air pump gets heated up. Can
you think why it is so? When we touch cold water, we feel cold, when we
touch boiling water we feel hot. What is such feeling of coldness and hotness
called? In first two cases, the mechanical energy is converted into the heat
energy. Similarly, the causes of feeling of hotness and coldness are due to
flow of something in the form of energy from one body to the other body. The
flow of energy from our body to the cold water has given us the feeling of
coldness. Similarly, the flow of energy from hot water to our body has given
feeling of hotness. Thus, the energy that flows from a hotter body to another
body producing the sensation of hotness and coldness is called heat. In
another word, heat can be defined as the form of energy which produces the
sensation of warmth.

Heat and Temperature

Molecular theory states that each object is made up of molecules and they are
in motion about their mean position. Hence, an object possesses kinetic
energy due to the motion of each molecule of the object.

When we heat an object the molecules presence in the object vibrate and the
kinetic energy of the molecules increases. So, average kinetic energy of the
molecules of a substance also increases. The average kinetic energy in the
molecules of hot object is more than in cold object. Hence, the quantity of
heat present in an object depends upon following two factors:

i. Number of molecules

 

ii, Average kinetic energy of the molecules

Thus, the heat contained in an object is directly linked to the kinetic energy of
its molecules. Hence, heat energy of an object is defined as the sum of the
kinetic energy that the molecules of an object posseses. It is measured by
using calorimeter and its S.L.unit is Joule(J).

When an object is heated, its temperature increases. It is due to the increase in
the kinetic energy of the molecules that form the object. According to kinetic
theory of molecules, the temperature of an object increases due to increase in
average kinetic energy of all the molecules of that object. The temperature of
an object is directly proportional to the molecular vibration of an object.

Science- 10 44


Heat and temperature are closely related. On heating a body, the heat energy
is absorbed by its molecules and the amount of heat as well as the temperature
(except during the change of state) of the body increase. Similarly, on cooling,
the temperature of a body decreases. Thus, heat is the cause of temperature
rise. Temperature is measured by an instrument named thermometer in any
standard unit °C, °F, K whereas heat is measured by calorimeter.

The temperature of the mixture of water is different than that of cold water
and hot water. The mixture has higher temperature than the cold water
whereas less temperature than that of hot water. Thus, heat flows from a body
at higher temperature to the one at lower temperature, until the temperature of
the two becomes the same irrespective of the quantities of heat present in two
bodies. In another way, if two systems are in thermal equilibrium then they
are at same temperature.

Thermometer and its structure

The branch of physics which deals with heat is called thermodynamics. A
device which is designed to measure temperature is called a thermometer. The
working principle of thermometer is based on the fact that a "body expands on

heating and contracts on cooling". In other words, the thermometer is based
on the property of thermal expansion of the thermometric used in it.

A general thermometer consists a glass stem with a fine and uniform hollow
capillary tube inside it. One end of the glass stem is sealed and at the other
end a thin walled bulb presents inside of which a thermometric liquid is kept.
The capillary tube provides space for the expansion of thermometric liquid
while measuring the temperature of a body. The glass stem is calibrated with
suitable thermometric scales.

The liquid that is used in thermometer is called thermometric liquid.
Generally mercury and alcohol are used as thermometric liquids. Let's have
brief discussion about these thermometric liquids.

Science- 10 46


Mercury

Mercury is only a metal that is in liquid state at room temperature which is
silvery, opaque and can easily be seen in capillary tube during its raise and
fall. It is good conductor of heat and is sensitive to heat as well which
expands and contracts uniformly in a wide range of temperature. Mercury
remains in liquid state over a wide range of temperature i.e. -39°C (freezing
point) to 357°C (boiling point). The mercury thermometer cannot be used to
measure the temperature in very cold regions.

Alcohol

Alcohol is cheaper, easily available and colorless thermometer liquid. Alcohol
expands sixth time more than mercury and hence it gives better accuracy than
mercury. The range of alcohol remains liquid to very low temperature
(freezing point -115°C) but not at higher temperature ic. beyond 78°C
(boiling point). Due to this reason, alcohol thermometer is used for measuring
the temperature in very cold regions.

Types of thermometer and their uses

On the basis of the structure, thermometer is classified into many types. They
are used for various purposes.

a) Clinical thermometer

The thermometer which is used to measure our body temperature is
known as clinical thermometer. A clinical thermometer is only used to
measure the temperature of human body. It consists of a long, narrow and
uniform glass tube with a bulb containing mercury at one end. It has a
kink in the fine capillary tube near the bulb to avoid the backward flow
of mercury when it is removed from the body. Hence, the accurate
temperature can be

Specific heat capacity

‘The heat energy is required to raise the temperature of a body. But different
amount of heat is required to change (increase or decrease) the temperature of
equal mass of different substances by 1°C. It is because heat capacity of
different substances is different. For example if equal mass of water and oil
are heated through 1°C, more heat energy is needed to raise the temperature
of water than oil. Thus, different quantity of heat is required to change the
temperature of equal mass of different substances.

Activity 4.4

Take two identical beakers of same
size and pour 500ml of water in any
of them and 500m! mustard oil in
another beaker. Set up the apparatus
as shown in the figure and measure
the temperature of the liquids in both
the beakers. Then heat them with

Note the temperature of both liquids
in every two minutes. Fig. 4.7

 

Out of these two liquids, whose temperature will rises faster? Why?

Though the same quantity of heat was given to both liquids, the temperature
of oil rises faster than that of water. This shows that different substances have
a property by virtue of which the same amount of heat supplied to them
causes difference in rise of temperature. As we know that substances are made
of molecules and the nature of molecules varies according to the substances.
The kinetic energy of the molecules of different substances is different even
though the same quantity of heat is supplied to them. This results the different
heat capacity of different substances,

The specific heat capacity of a substance is the amount of heat required to
raise the temperature of 1kg of a substance through 1 'C.

It has been experimentally proved that 4200 joules of heat energy is required
to raise the temperature of Ikg of water through 1'' C. Hence, the specific heat
capacity of water is 4200J/kg °C.

be

Specific heat capacity determines the heat absorbing capacity of a substance.
A body having high specific capacity can absorb or lose more amount of heat
but a substance having less specific heat capacity can absorb or lose less
amount of heat quickly.

Heat Equation

During the thermal contact, quantity of heat lost by a hot body is always equal
to the quantity of heat gained by another body if heat lost by radiation is
neglected. It is based on the law of conservation of energy.

So, Heat lost = Heat gained
Heat lost or gained by a body is directly proportional to its mass, if change in
temperature is kept constant Le. Q am. .@

Again, the quantity of heat lost or gained by a body is directly proportional to
its temperature difference if mass is constant.

 

 

From relation (i) and (ii), we get
Qamdt
Q=msdt

Where 's' is proportionality constant and also known as the specific heat
capacity of the body.

This equation is called heat equation. Therefore, heat equation states that the
quantity of heat lost or gained by a body is equal to the product of mass,
specific heat capacity and temperature difference of the body.

Summary

1. Heat is the sum of kinetic energy of molecules of a body and temperature
arises due to increase in average kinetic energy of these molecules.

2. The mass and temperature of a body determine the amount of heat in it.

3. Temperature can be measured with different scales such as Celsius,
Fahrenheit and Kelvin.

4. Heat is measured by a calorimeter and temperature is measured by a
thermometer.

5. A thermometer works on the principle of thermal expansion.
6. Liquid used in a thermometer can either be alcohol or mercury.

7. The amount of heat required to raise the temperature of 1 kg of a
substance by 1°C is called specific heat capacity.

8. Due to high specific heat capacity of water it is widely used for heating as
well as cooling purposes.

9. The quantity of heat lost or gained by a body is equal to the product of
mass, specific heat capacity and temperature differences of the body. icc.
Q=msdt.

Glossary

Kinetic molecular theory: the theory which explains the physical properties
of matter in terms of the motion of its constituent
particles

Thermal equilibrium: —_ condition at which two substances in contact are
at same temperature

Thermal expansion: tendency of matter to change its dimension in
response to temperature

Science- 10 56


uot LIGHT

How do we see objects around us during day but unable to see them at night?
What is the type of energy that makes objects visible? Do you have any friends or
family members who use spectacles? Do you know any specific reason behind the
use of spectacles? Let’s have discussion,

Light makes all the objects around us visible. Light is a form of energy which
gives us the sensation of vision. Light itself is invisible but it makes objects
visible. As the light coming from its source strike on the objects, it gets reflected
When these reflected rays reach to the retina of our eye, its image is formed on the
retina, Image thus formed reaches to our brain through optical nerve and objects
become visible. If the eyes have defect then the image can’t be formed on the
retina, To overcome this problem, a lens of suitable power is used which we
commonly called spectacles.

In our daily life, we use different types of optical instruments. All these
instruments are provided with lenses. In this chapter, we are going to study about
lens, phenomenon of refraction of light by lens and defects of vision.

Lens

Have you ever used binoculars to see distant objects? Have you noticed the lens
used in mobile and watch repair centre to see their minute parts clearly? What do
these instruments have? These instruments have lens. It is an useful device used in
various optical instruments. A lens is a piece of transparent glass bounded by two
refracting surfaces which are usually spherical in shape. It is usually made up of
glass. Spherical lenses can be classified into two types : convex lens and concave
Tens.

Convex lens

The lens which is thick at the middle and thin at the edge is called convex lens. It
converges a parallel beam of light at a point after refracting through it. That's why
it is called converging lens. Depending upon the position of the objects it can
produce real as well as virtual images. It can also produce magnified as well as
diminished images. Biconvex, plano-convex, concavo convex are the types of
convex lens. There is biconvex lens in human eyes.

Science- 10 57


Fig. 5.1: Converging lens

Concave lens: The lens which is thin at the middle and thick at the edges is called
concave lens. It diverges the parallel beam of light after refracting through it
That's why it is called diverging lens. This lens always produces virtual and
diminished image. Biconcave, plano concave, canvexo concave are the types of
concave lens.

 

Fig. 5.2: Diverging lens

Lens as a group of prisms

A lens is supposed to be made up of combination of many prisms. A convex
lens is also made up of a set of prisms in such a way that the prisms in the
upper half have their bases downwards and the prisms in the lower half have
their bases upwards. The central parts

of the lens are just like a thick glass

slab as in figure 5.3. The rays of light

after refracting through the lens

always bend towards its base. So the E
prism in the upper part of the lens

bends the incident ray downward,

while the prism in the lower part of

the lens bends the incident ray — Convexlens Fig. 53

slab. So the light passes through it without deviation. That’s why a convex
lens converses the rays of light after refraction.

Similarly, a concave lens is also made by
the combination of prisms in such a way awa

the lens, which is just like a rectangular glass slab, so the light passes through
it without deviation. Thus, a concave lens diverges the rays of light after
refraction.

Some terms related to lens

Different specific terms are used while discussing about the function of lenses.
Centre of curvature, principal axis, optical center, principal focus, focal length are
such important terms and are defined as follow.

Center of curvature

The centre of the sphere of which the lens is a part is called centre of curvature.
There are two spherical surfaces in the lens. So, there are two centres of curvature
Cy and Cy as shown in figure.

 

  

Principal axis

The line joining both the centers of curvature of a lens is called the principal
axis, In both of the above figures, XY represents the principal axis.

Science- 10 59


Optical centre

The geometrical centre of a lens is known as its optical centre. In the given
figure, the point O represents the optical centre. A ray of light passing through
it remains undeviated.

Principal focus or focus

Principal focus is the point on the principal axis where the rays of light
parallel to the principal axis converge after refraction through a convex lens or
appears to diverge from a point on the principal axis through a concave lens.
In the figure, the point F represents the focus.

Focal length

The distance between the
optical centre (O) and the
principal focus (F) of a
lens is called its focal
length. It is denoted by
letter 'f. Focal length of
a lens depends on its
thickness. A thick lens
has shorter focal length than a thin lens. In diagram, the distance between O and F
is focal length.

 

 

Activity 5.1 Method of determining focal length of a convex lens

Hold convex lens and keep it in front of distant objects like tree, house ete. Then
put a paper behind the lens. Make to face the rays of light from the distant object
on the paper. Now shift the lens towards or a way from the paper until clear
inverted image of distant object is obtained. Measure the distance between the
lens and paper. Then you will get the focal length of that lens.

When parallel rays from the distance object incident as a convex lens, it produces
image on its focus after refraction. This fact is used while determining the focal
length of a convex lens. In this process, paper is shifted towards and way from the
lens to produce clear image on the paper. The process of adjusting distance
between the lens and the screen to produce clear image on the screen is called
focusing. Focusing is necessary to get clear and distinct image from any optical
instruments.

Science- 10 60


Rule of refraction through lens

1. The ray parallel to the principal axis passes through the principal focus after
refracting through the lens.

2. The ray passing through the optical centre does not deviate.

3. The incident ray passing through the principal focus becomes parallel to the
principal axis after refraction through the lens.

Power of lens

The power of a lens is its ability to converge (in convex lens) or diverge (in
concave lens) the incident beam of light. The power is said to be positive if the
lens converges the rays and negative if it diverges. The ability of lens to converge
or diverge the incident beam of light is inversely proportional to its focal length.
Shorter the focal length, the greater is the convergence or divergence produced by
alens.

  

Mathematically, it is the reciprocal of its focal length expressed in meter.
P= ; (where f is expressed in meter)

The power of lens is measured in diopter (D). Diopter is also measured in radian
/meter.

Human eye

Human eye is the natural optical instrument which produces real images. It
consists of flexible convex lens and it helps to see the objects around us. Since,
human eye is delicate organ so it is being protected inside the cavity of the skull.

Science- 10 66


The rays of the light from an object pass
through cornea, aqueous humour, pupil, lens, ( ane
vitreous humorous and then converge in retina
forming its image. The image formed on the
retina is real and inverted. Optical nerves carry
this information to the brain and brain inverts
and interprets the image. retina

Fig. 5.17

‘optic

 

Accommodation of eye

The process by which cilliary muscles function to change the focal length of the
eye lens so that the image formed on the retina becomes clear is called the
accommodation of the eye. It varies for near and distant objects and also for
moving away or towards the eye. By adjusting the focal length, the eye is actually
changing its lens power. Thus, the automatic ability of the lens of the eyes to
adjust its focal length to form the image of objects on retina is called
accommodation of eyes.

Range of vision

The power of accommodation possessed by an eye with normal vision is such that
it can clearly see the object placed anywhere between infinity and its near point.
The nearest point from the eyes at which an object can be seen clearly by the eyes
is called its near point. The near point of a normal eye is at a distance of 25cm
from the eye. It is the minimum distance for the eye beyond which an eye can
accommodate and focus object clearly. So, if an object is placed at a distance less
than 25cm from the normal eyes, the power of accommodation is not possible and
the image is formed beyond retina.

The farthest point from the eye at which an object can be seen clearly by the eye is
called the far point of the eye. For a normal eye, the far point is at infinity. Thus,
the distance between near point to far point which can be focused by our eyes is
called range of vision. The normal eyes can focus the objects lying inside the
range of vision.

Defects of vision

A normal eye can see clearly the objects lying anywhere between 25cm and
infinity from the eye. Thus, the image of an object lying anywhere between 25cm
and infinity is formed on the retina. An eye which fails to do so is said to be
defective. The eye which can’t see object placed at short distance or long distance
is said to have a defect of vision. Generally, there are two types of defect of vision
and they are categorised as

a. Short sightedness (Myopia) b. Long sightedness (Hypermetropia)

Science- 10 67


Short sightedness (Myopia)

The defect of vision in which a person can sec the nearby object but cannot see
the distant objects clearly is called myopia. For such person the farthest point is
nearer than infinity. So in this defect of vision, the image of the distant object is
formed in front of the retina. This defect of vision arises due to the following
cause.

© Due to the decrease in focal length of the eye lens or
© Duc to the elongation of eye ball.

Eyes suffering from myopia has eye lens thicker than the normal one. So the
image of distant objects form infront of retina. This type of defect of vision can be
corrected by wearing spectacles with concave lens of suitable power. Concave
lens diverges the parallel rays of light and help the lens of the eye to produce clear
image on the retina.

Concave lens

     

Image roma
distant abject

    

Fig. 5.18

Long sightedness (Hypermetropia)

The defect of vision in which a person can see distant objects but cannot see
nearby objects clearly is called hypermetropia. For such person near point moves
away beyond 25cm. So in this defect of vision, the image of the nearby object is
formed behind the retina. This defect of vision arises due to the following cause.

© Due to increase in focal length of eye lens or
* Due to shortening of eye ball.

Eyes suffering from hypermetropia has eye lens thinner than the normal. So the
image of distant objects get formed beyond of retina. This type of defect of vision
can be corrected by wearing spectacles with convex lens of suitable power.
Convex lens converges the parallel rays of light and help the lens of the eye to
produce clear image on the retina.

1.

6.

Light is a form of energy that gives us the sensation of vision.

Lens is a piece of transparent glass bounded by two refracting surfaces which
are usually spherical in shape.

Concave lens is thin at middle and thick at edge while convex lens is thick at
middle and thin at edges.

A concave lens always produces virtual, erect and diminished image but
convex lens produces both real and virtual as well as diminished and
magnified images.

The magnification produced by a lens is defined as the ratio of size of image
to the size of object.

The converging and diverging capacity of a lens is called its power. Power of
lens is measured in Dioptre (D).

The ability of an eye to focus the image of objects at various distances on the
retina by changing the focal length of the eye lens is called accommodation
of eye.

 

The nearest point that can be focused clearly by the normal eye is called near
point.

Myopia is the defect of vision in which a person can see nearby objects but
cannot see the distant objects clearly.

. Hypermetropia is the defect of vision in which a person can see distant

objects but cannot see nearby objects clearly.

Science- 10 2


Current Electricity

ems and Magnetism

Nowadays, current electricity has been regarded as the main source of energy. For
what purpose the electricity is being used? Which equipment can be run by using
electricity? Think how people are using electricity in their daily life. Today, in
this global world, use of electricity is being widen. Science and technology has
made the impossible things possible to happen. Electric appliances like fan,
television, computer, heater, washing machine, etc. are operated using electricity.
Current Electricity is transformed into different forms of energy which help to
perform different tasks. Electroplating of gold and silver is also done by using
electricity. It is also used to run industries.

In this chapter we will study about electricity, its effects, appliances used in our
daily life and consumption of electricity.

Effect of Current electricity

When electric current flows through a certain conductor the electric energy gets
transformed into various forms such as heat, light, sound, chemical, etc. The
transformation of electric energy into other forms is a result of effect of
electricity. Let's discuss some effects of electricity.

Heating effect

When electric current is passed through a conductor having high resistance, it gets
heated up. This affect is known as heating effect of electricity. The heat energy
produced in the conductor depends upon magnitude of electric current passed
through it, its resistance and time for which electricity flows through the
conductor. The conductor which converts electrical energy into heat energy is
called heating element. Nichrome is used as heating element in common practice.
It is an alloy of nickel (60%) and chromium (40%). It has very high resistance as
well as high melting point and it doesn’t react with oxygen of air even at higher
temperature about 900° C .So, it easily converts electrical energy into heat energy.

 

Electric heater, immersion rod, rice cooker, electric iron, electric kettle are some
examples of electric appliances based on heating effect of electricity.

Science- 10 B


 

Iron Heater Imersion heater Electric ketle

Lighting effect

When current is passed through a wire of high resistance, it becomes extremely
hot and produces light. This effect is called lighting effect of electric current. Such
effect of current is used for glowing electric lamps. The devices which are used to
convert electrical energy into light and heat energy are called lighting devices.

  

Filament lamp

An electric lamp in which filament is used to
convert electrical energy into light energy is called
filament lamp. It consists of a coil made up of thin a
wire enclosed in a glass bulb with inert gases like Nuopen a,
argon, neon or nitrogen which is connected to ate
terminal made up of lead via thick wire as shown in sgnngue_|-___/,
the figure. When current passes through the stare
filament, it becomes very hot (nearly up to 2900°C)

due to its high resistance. As the filament becomes

white hot due to high temperature, it emits visible

light.

The filament is generally made up of tungsten metal. It has high resistivity and
high melting point about 3400°C. When the filament comes in contact with
oxygen at high temperature; it gets destroyed due to oxidation. Therefore, inert or
inactive gas such as argon, neon or nitrogen is filled in the filament lamp.

 

The filament lamp emits more heat than light energy. It connects only about 10 %
of the electrical energy into light energy and remaining 90% is wasted as heat
energy. The average life span of filament lamp is about 1000 hours.

Fluorescent lamp

   

A fluorescent lamp is a device which converts electrical
energy into light energy with the help of mercury vapor
and fluorescent powder. It consists of a long cylindrical

tube which contains fluorescent power coated in its Eicon
Fluorescent amp

Tubeleht stare)
ucrecent Pouce” AC 220 v
ao

 

Science- 10 74


inner wall. Two electrodes are fixed at the ends and is sealed with mercury vapor
at low pressure. The electrodes are provided with two external leads for
connecting to power supply. When current flows through electrodes, electrons
flow from one electrode to another electrode through mercury vapour and the
mercury atoms collide with electrons. Then it produces invisible ultra-violet rays.
When the ultra-violet rays fall on the fluorescent power coated on the inner walls
of glass tube, visible light is emitted. The color of light thus emitted can be
changed by changing the colour of fluorescent powder.

A fluorescent lamp is much efficient than a filament lamp. It converts about 30%
of electric energy into light energy and about 70% into heat energy. It is more
durable as its life span is about 3000 hours.

Do you know?

Compact fluorescent lamp (CFL) is more efficient than simple fluorescent lamp. It
can convert 90% of electrical energy into light.

LED
ALLED lamp is a light emitting diode which is assembled into a lamp (light bulb)
for the uses of lighting fixtures. LED lamps have a life span and electrical
efficiency which are several times greater than ordinary lamps and are
significantly more efficient than fluorescent lamps.

LEDs have many advantages over incandescent light sources, including lower
energy consumption, longer life, improved physical robustness, smaller size and
faster switching. Light emitting diodes (IED) are used in the applications like
automotive headlamps, adverting, general lighting, traffic signals, camera flashes
etc. It converts 90% of electrical energy into light.

Hans Christian Oersted discovered the
magnetic effect of current in the year 1819.
He observed the deflection of magnetic
needle of compass when it was bought near Raa

When an electric current is passed through a wire, a magnetic field is produced
around it. This is known as magnetic effect of current. Its application is very
popular day by day as it is applied in various electronic appliances like
microphone, loud speaker, radio and television.

Science- 10 75


Electric Bell

An electric bell is a device which converts electric
energy into the sound energy. It consists of a U-shaped
soft iron core around which an insulated wire is wound.
A soft iron plate is adjusted in front of the
electromagnet. The flexible plate is connected with
hammer, It also bears a sound producing gong.

When the switch is put on, iron bar acquires a
temporary magnetism and the flexible plate of magnetic
material is attracted towards it due to which the
hammer hits the gong and the bell rings. As the plate
moves toward the magnet, the circuit breaks. So, the
iron core losses its magnetic property and the plate
returns to the original position and again the circuit
becomes closed and the same process repeats, Due to this repeated action, bell
rings continuously.

 

It is used as doorbell at home, as indicator in school and office etc.

Bicycle Dynamo

 

A very small and simple dynamo is used in
bicycle to light its bulb. It works on the principle
that a moving magnet near a wire in a circuit
induces an electric current. It is made up of a coil i
of insulated wire, permanent bar magnet, driving — wheelot bicycle
wheel, etc.

 

 

 

 

 

 

 

A powerful permanent magnet is kept closer to a coil whereas the driving wheel is
kept in contact with the bicycle wheel. When wheel of the bicycle rotates the
driving wheel along with bar magnet spins with high speed. This coil cuts the
magnetic lines of force and finally produces current in the coil which helps to
glow the bulb kept in the handle of the bicycle.

speed by using external force. The rotor
fixed with the electromagnet rotates along
with the turbine. As a result current is --
induced in the coil due to the change in
the magnetic flux linked to the coil.

iv. By reducing the distance between magnet and the coil

Electric appliances and their uses
Inverter

The term inverter was first introduced by
David Chandler Prince in 1925 AD.
Inverter is an electric device which
converts alternating current (a.c) into
direct current (d.c). It contains a special

 

Science- 10 78


device called diod which lets the current flow in only one direction. Inverter
converts direct current (d.c) into alternating current (a.c). It usually comes with
battery which stores electrical energy so that it can be used when there is no
power supply.

Charger

The electrical device which is used to charge rechargeable battery is called a
charger. Some of the devices come with inbuilt battery. One end of the charger is
connected to the battery or the device with battery and another end is connected to
the supply of the current. As electric current is passed into the device, the battery
gets charged. The device has its own cut off system. Due to this system, the
charging of the battery stops itself when the battery is fully charged. It is used to
charge mobile, emergency light, radio etc.

Adapter

An AC adapter is a small power supply that changes household voltage of
alternating current (AC) in to low voltage DC, making suitable for the electronic
devices. Adapter allows one hardware or electronic interface. It is used to run
radio and other electrical appliances that need low voltage.

Solar Cell

Solar cell is a device that converts light energy directly into the electrical energy
by the voltaic effect. A solar cell, previously called solar battery is an example of
a photovoltaic device. A photovoltaic device is a device that generates voltage
when exposed to light. It was discovered by Alexander Edmond Becquerel in
1839.

Solar module is the major component used to convert sunlight into electricity.
Conductors and the most semi conductors are used in it. The common semi —
conductor used is silicon crystal, which is laminated into n-type and p-type layers.
These layers are kept one after another. When light strikes these crystals, it
induces “photovoltaic effect” and electricity is produced. The electricity so
produced can be used immediately or it can also be stored in a battery.

Working Mechanism of Solar Cells

1. Photons in sunlight stroked on the solar panel are absorbed by the semi-
conductors used (silicon).

2. With the collision of photon, electrons in the semi-conductors get excited from
their atomic orbital.

3. Excited electrons release energy to return to their original orbital, During the
process current is captured by electrode.

Science- 10 79


4. Solar cell converts solar energy into a Direct Current (DC).

5. An inverter can convert the DC into Alternating Current (AC).

Direct Current (DC) and Alternating Current (AC)

The electric current in which polarity/direction and magnitude do not change
periodically is called direct current. It is produced by cells or battery.

Magnitude
Magnitude

Time Time

Alternating Current Direct Current

The electric current in which polarity/direction and magnitude change periodically
is called alternating current (AC). For example, the frequency of the alternating
current distributed in Kathmandu is 50Hz. It means polarity of current in
Kathmandu changes /alternates at the rate of 50 times per second. AC is produced
by generator and AC dynamo

Transformer

A transformer is an electric device which converts low a.c voltage to high a.c
voltage or vice-versa. It is based on the principle of mutual induction i.e. when an
alternating current is passed in one coil and induced current is produced in the
neighboring coil. The coil in which a.c current is fed is known as primary coil and
the voltage supplied to the primary coil is called primary voltage. The coil of the
transformer from which electric current is trapped out is called a secondary coil.
The voltage of the secondary coil is called secondary voltage. The current
supplied to the transformer is called input current and the current drawn from the
secondary coil of the transformer is called output current.

A transformer consists of a laminated soft iron core made up of thin frames of soft
iron placed one above the another and insulated from each other by a chemical
called varnish or shellac. The lamination of the soft iron core is done to prevent
the loss of energy in the form of heat. There is an important relationship between
the ratio of the number of turns of primary coils and that of secondary coil with
the primary and secondary voltage.

There are two types of transformers.
i) Step up transformer

The transformer which converts low ac voltage in to high ac
voltage (ic. Vp<Vs) is called step up transformer. It has more
turns in secondary coil than that in primary coil (Np<Ns). It is
used in electric grids to save power during transmission through
overhead wires.

 

ii) Step down transformer

The transformer which converts high ac voltage to low ac
voltage (i.e. Vp>Vs) is called step down transformer. It has
less turns in secondary coil than that in the primary i.e.
Np2Ns. It is used in the house to step down the high voltage
current to low voltage up to 240V or 220V. It is also used in
electric appliances to get further smaller voltage.
