Environmental Pollution and
Management

Unit 20

You have seen many people suffering from various diseases such as typhoid,
cholera, dysentery, eye infection, infection of respiratory parts, skin diseases,
and even some fatal diseases like cancer. These diseases are spreading at an
alarming rate these days. Do you know the reason behind the terrific increase
of such diseases?

Environment is the surrounding around us. It includes all the biotic and
abiotic components. The biotic components include plants and animals where
as abiotic components include all the non-living factors such as soil, air,
water, light etc. Balanced environment helps every creatures of the earth to
live their life in a happy and healthy manner. But the unbalanced and polluted
environment disturbs everyone’s life and causes hazards. Over population
growth, industrialization, urbanization etc. are the major causes behind
environmental pollution, which is the undesired spread of toxic chemicals into
the physical and biological components of the environment. Pollution usually
affects multiple systems. It causes hardships to plants, animals and other
organisms. Contamination of air, water and soil causes the spreading of
various diseases. Industries and factories are releasing many harmful gases
into the environment. If it continues, the amount of carbon monoxide and
carbon dioxide get increased in the air. As a result, the temperature of the
earth increases.

 

     

In this chapter, we are going to discuss on the causes, effects and mitigating
measures of air pollution, water pollution and soil pollution.

Air pollution

Air pollution is the entrance of harmful substances into the atmosphere. It
may cause diseases, allergies and even the death of humans. It also harms
other animals, plants and destroys the natural environment. The harmful
substances that cause pollution are called pollutants. Air pollutants are usually
carbon monoxide, carbon dioxide, sulphur dioxide, oxides of nitrogen
expelled from high temperature combustion. Similarly, methane, toxic metals
like lead and mercury, chlorofluorocarbons released from air conditions,
refrigerators, odours from garbage, sewage and nuclear explosions are also
the main air pollutants.

243


Sources of air pollution

1. Natural sources: These are the sources usually occur in the nature. For
example, volcanic explosion, forest fire, soil erosion, ete.

 

2. Artificial sources: These are the artificial or manmade sources
like carbon monoxide, carbon dioxide, ammonia, oxides of nitrogen,
sulphur dioxide, chlorine etc. Most of them are released from the
factories and industries while burning the things. Mobile sources like
motor vehicles, aircrafts, fumes from paint, spray, waste deposition
which generate methane cause air pollution.

Effects of air pollution

Air pollution is a significant risk factor for a number of pollution related
diseases and health, Some major effects of air pollution are given below.

 

The minute solid particles like carbon enter into our body and become
the major cause of lung diseases. These particles settle on the plants and
disturb photosynthesis.

ii, Unburned fuels cause the production of carbon monoxide. It is extremely
poisonous. It mixes with the blood and prevents it from carrying oxygen.
It may cause the death of a person.

iii. Excess carbon dioxide in the air causes green house effect. Other gases
that cause the effect are nitrous oxide, methane, sulphur dioxide,
chlorofluorocarbons, etc. Collection of these gases in the atmosphere
blocks the solar radiations to return back and causes global warming.
This can cause large scale melting of ice in the polar reasons leading to
flooding of coastal areas by sea water.

iv. Distant objects cannot be seen because of the accumulation of smoke and
gases in the air. Visibility degradation is caused by the absorption and
scattering of light by particles and gases in the air. Hence, air pollution
causes reduction in visibility.

y. Chlorofluorocarbons, methyl chloroform, carbon tetrachloride like gases
damage the ozone layer. It causes an increase in the amount of ultraviolet
rays from the sun reaching the earth. The uv rays causes eyes and skin
diseases to the human beings.

vi. Climate change is caused due to air pollution. It results extreme cold
during winter and extreme hot during summer.

vii, Polluted air causes various airborne diseases to the human beings. It
adversely affects the respiratory tract. It causes eyes infection, bronchitis,

244


heart diseases, and cancer. It also causes disturbed sleep, weakness,
irritation etc. The lead present in the air is absorbed by our body which
causes mental disorder.

viii. Sulphur dioxide and oxides of nitrogen cause damage of leaves of the
plants. Dust particles deposited on the leaf of plants reduce
photosynthesis. The reduction of photosynthesis decreases productivity
of plants.

Measures to control air pollution

i. Industries, factories and chimneys are established far from the settlement
areas. The harmful gases given off should pass through water before they
are released out. This helps the poisonous gases like SO, NO> to be
dissolved in the water.

ii, Use of specially designed smokeless stoves for buming coal, kerosene
etc. should be practiced.

iii, Afforestation reduces the air pollution.

iv. Use of alternative energy sources like solar energy, hydroelectricity etc.
y. Controlling rapid population growth.

vi. Manage legal provision and creating awareness.

vii. Banning old vehicles.

Water pollution

Water is the most abundant substance on the earth’s surface. It exists in the
three states solid, liquid and gas. Pure water is tasteless and odorless. Water
is very essential for all the organisms to live. River, springs, lakes, ponds,
wells, etc. are the sources of water. But water of all these sources is getting
polluted day by day. Wastes discharged from industries, hospitals and homes
cause the water resources polluted. Water pollution is the undesired change in
the original quality of water that adversely affects the health of humans and
other organisms.

Sources of water pollution

Human activities are mainly responsible for water pollution. Some major
sources are given below:

1. The disposal of sewage water to the rivers, streams, and other sources
cause water pollution. It degrades the quality of water.

245


2. The wastes produced in the industries and factories, various chemicals
and papers are disposed in the water sources.

3. Excessive use of pesticides and insecticides causes water pollution. They
are used in the crop field. During raining, rain water carries these
chemicals into the water resources which degrade the quality of water.

4, Natural disasters like flood, soil erosion, heavy rainfall, etc. causes water
pollution.

5. Sudden bursting of drainage pipe and leakage cause water pollution.

6. Washing clothes, bathing cattles, cleaning utensils near water sources can
cause water pollution.

7. Nuclear test in the water sources cause water pollution.
Measures to control water pollution

1. Wastes produced at homes, industries and factories should be disposed
properly. The wastes produced at the hospitals, industries, etc. should be
treated well before they are discharged.

2. Adopting effective control of flood, landslide by constructing check
dams,

Using biodegradable fertilizers and pesticides.
4. Reducing chemical fertilizer run off into the sources of water.
Banning nuclear test in the water sources.
6. Proper management of drainage system.
7. Tree plantation.
8. Reducing the use of excessive chemical fertilizers and pesticides.
Soil pollution

Soil pollution is the degradation of quality of the soil due to the presence of
wastes. With the rise of building and roads, soil pollution has highly
increased. It is mainly due to manmade wastes. The waste produced from the
nature itself such as dead plant, rotten parts etc. only add to the fertility of
soil. However, manmade wastes are full of chemicals that are not naturally
found and lead to soil pollution.

246


Main causes of soil pollution

1.

Industrial wastes are the major soil pollutants. The wastes include
chemicals, metals and non-metals, contaminated things, etc. Such wastes
reduce the fertility of soil as well as harm the human health.

There is the excessive use of chemicals to destroy the insects and pests
that destroy our crops. They reduce the fertility of soil. Some chemicals
damage the composition of the soil and make it easier to erode by water
and air.

A growing cause of soil pollution is the disposal of waste water. The
contaminated water from the industries and factories degrade quality of
soil. The urine and feces disposed into the field causes soil pollution.

Acid rain is caused due to the mixing up of the chemicals with the rain
and fall down on the ground. The acid containing rain water dissolves
many nutrients in the soil and changes the structure of the soil.

People use various things at home in their life. The things become wastes
after they are used for a long time. Dust, papers, utensils, metals, plastics,
rotten fruits and vegetables, etc. are the waste products. When these
things are thrown in the land, they cause the degradation of the soil.

Fertilizers are used to increase the crop production. Excessive deposition
and use of these chemicals cause the reduction of the fertility of soil.

Measures to control soil pollution

1.

eID

Use of such pesticides which kills the harmful pests and insects but does
not contaminate the soil with toxic chemicals.

Pesticides and insecticides should be used in a limited amount in the
agricultural field only as recommended by the experts.

There should be the gap between the harvesting of crops and spray of
pesticides. It reduces the contamination of crops.

Education to the farmers for regarding the use of pesticides and
fertilizers.

Regular observation of soil nutrients.
Waste water from industries should not be used for irrigation.
Adopting soil conservation practices.

Adopting solid waste management programmes.

247


Conservation and management of forest

Forest is a region with a large number of trees, herbs, shrubs, etc. It is the
habitat of different wild lives. The parts of the plant that undergo decaying
process mix with the soil and increase the fertility of soil. Forest preserves
watersheds. It helps to balance the rainfall pattern. Many medicinal herbs are
found in the forest.

Conservation of forest includes the following points.

1.

awPryvnd

Afforestation in the hilly and sloppy regions.
Control forest fire.

Formulation and effective practice of rules and regulations.
Overgrazing should be controlled.

Launching community forest programme.

Wise use of forest products.

Conservation and management of sources of water

Water is an important natural resource.
Life is not possible without water.
Water is used for drinking, washing
clothes, bathing, irrigation, generating
electricity, running industries etc. Some
of the methods of water conservation
are as follows.

unea History of the Earth

The earth is only the planet in the solar system that is suitable for survival of
living organisms including human civilization. The earth is about 4.55 billion
years old, There are several hypothesis about the origin of the earth. Some of
them are as follows:

1.

George Wofan hypothesis (Planetesimal hypothesis)

In 1745, George Wofan put forward a theory of origin of earth,
According to this hypothesis a comet moving around the universe
crashed with the sun, the splashed matter from the sun resulted the
formation of our earth along with other planets and satellites.

Nebular or Kant hypothesis

In 1755, a German philosopher Kant proposed another theory of origin of
earth. According to this hypothesis, the whole of our solar system
including all the heavenly bodies were in an extremely large mass of gas
and dust known as nebula which was nearly circular and was spinning
slowly from west to east. Due to mutual gravitation, particles of nebula
started to be collected at different places. Large mass collected at the
centre of the nebula ultimately became Sun and other small masses
collected at different places became planets, asteroids, satellites, etc. The
spinning motion of the nebula converted into revolutionary motion of
these heavenly bodies around the sun. But in 1796, Laplace modified this
hypothesis. According to him, the Nebula started to gradual cooling and
contraction, resulted into continuous decrease in the size and volume of
Nebula and became a large and loose ball of dust and gases. During this
process, several outer ring formed and detached from the centre one after
another and started to revolve around the centre. The masses in the ring
began to change into planets and satellites while the central core became
the sun.

Tidal or Jean and Jaffery hypothesis

In 1919, Jean and Jaffery proposed another hypothesis. According to this
hypothesis, the sun was a very big and extensive mass of gas which was
moving in space. A big comet came closer to the sun and the
gravitational force of the comet attracted the sun, then the molten mass of

the sun was elongated toward the comet forming tides. As the star moved
away from the sun, some parts of the tide broke down into number of

251


pieces, which became planet and satellite. Finally they began to revolve
around the sun.

Some facts about our earth:

Estimated age:

4.55 billion years

Mass: 6 x 1071 metric tons
Total surface area: 509, 700, 000 km?
Land area: 148, 400,000 km?
Water area: 361, 300, 000 km?
Highest land: 8848 m (Mt. Everest)
Lowest point: 399m (Dead sea)
Average density: 55 gm/em’

Number of satellite: 1 (Moon)

Geological time scale

Geologists have prepared a geological timetable of the earth. The geological
history has been divided into eons, eras, periods and epochs. We shall study
the history of earth only on the basis of era.

The whole geological time scale is divided into four eras. They are,

lL.

= PF wd

Pre Cambrian era
Paleozoic era
Mesozoic era
Cenozoic era

Pre Cambrian era

Pre Cambrian era began about 4.5 billion years ago and ended 570
million years ago. It is actually the combination of Archeozoic (or
Archean), Proterozoic and Eozoic era. The early part of this era is the
beginning of the carth. Some major events of this era are as follows,

a. Metamorphic rocks were formed from igneous rocks.
b. Formation of atmosphere, hydrosphere and lithosphere took place.

c.  Unicellular and multicellular organisms were evolved in shallow
sea that had nearly surrounded the whole earth.

252


 

d. Very primitive bacteria were evolved.
Paleozoic era

Paleozoic era began from 570 millions years ago to 250 millions years
ago. Different terrestrial plants developed in this era so this era can be
termed as the era of big ferns. Major events of this era were as follows:

Sedimentary rocks were formed.

a.
b. Climate change and change in atmosphere took place.

2

Aquatic and terrestrial vertebrates and invertebrates were evolved.

d. Different bryophytes and pteriodophytes were evolved. Fern plant
upto 25ft and club mos upto 100ft were evolved in this era.

Mesozoic era

Mesozoic era began 250 million years ago and ended some 65 million
years ago. This era was dominated by giant reptiles like dinosaurs. The
main events of this era are given below.

a. Hills and mountains were formed.
b. Climate became suitable for aquatic, terrestrial and aerial animals.

c. The giant reptiles like dinosaurs evolved, flourished and were
extinct.

d. Coniferous plants were developed.
e. Mammals began to evolve at the end of this era.
Cenozoic era

Cenozoic era began 65 million years ago and still going on. This era is
also known as era of human beings. Human dominance began in this era.
The main events of this era are given below.

a. Expansion and breaking down of rocks took place.

b. The temperature of the earth decreased and the climate changed
drastically.

c. Mountains were covered with snow due to decrease in temperature.

d. The process of extinction of ancient animals and plants and
evolution of new animals and plants continued in this era.

253


Evolution of life

Our carth is formed about 4.55 billion years ago but its climatic condition was
not suitable for any living things because it was too hot. Slowly as the earth
cooled down, water vapour in the atmosphere condensed and rain fall took
place. Then oceans formed, almost 4.4 billion years ago. Because of the
unfavorable surface condition, the most likely place for life to develop might
have been at deep ocean where the very basic need for life would have been
available. So, it was only 3.8 billions years ago, unicellular bacteria developed
and 3.2 billion years ago, algae developed. In this way evolution of life began.
But in the course, various kinds of organisms were evolved, dominated the
earth and became extinct.

Scientists knew all about evolution, domination and extinction of organisms
with the help of the impressions of hard part of their bodies on the rocks that
are known as fossils. After the in-depth study and analysis of these fossils
scientists discovered various events that took place in different eras and
finally compiled the process of evolution of life on earth.

In Archean era (Pre-chambrian = Archean era + Proterozoic ear), no life had
evolved since no sedimentary rocks were formed. In Proterozoic era,
unicellular organisms were evolved and some multicellular organisms were
developed later. In Paleozoic era, lots of changes in weather took place and
gradually the climatic condition of the earth became favorable for living
organisms so different types of aquatic as well as terrestrial animals such as
fishes, amphibians and some early reptiles evolved. In Mesozoic era, the
change in climate continued. Giant reptiles like dinosaurs and toothed bird,
evolved, developed and also became extinct. This era is also known as age of
reptiles since big, giant reptiles dominated this era. In Cenozoic era, early
humans evolved. Many mammals like cat, rat, dog, bat, elephant, etc. evolved
and developed.

Fossils

The impression of part or whole body of animals and plants on sedimentary
rocks that are buried in the earth crust over a long period of time is called
fossils. The branch of science that deals with the study of fossils is known as
paleontology.

Process of fossils formation

Fossils are formed only on the sedimentary rocks because formation of fossils
and sedimentary rocks take place simultaneously in the same event.

254


Due to natural disasters such as volcanoes, floods and earthquakes, dead
plants and animals get buried under the surface of the earth. Then, the delicate
and soft parts of plants and animals decay while the hard parts remain in the
soil. The process of pressing down of these parts by the soil above them
continued in the ground for a very long time and finally the external
morphology of these hard parts are formed on the soil which by then have
changed into sedimentary rock. In this way, fossils are formed.

Identification of fossils

Fossils identification is a challenging task because even a small detail should
be studied and analysed very carefully, since that small detail separates one
species from another. Fossils are identified by studying the impressions left
on the rocks. They are also identified by studying the structure and
morphology of parts or whole body of living organisms casted on the rocks.
They are also identified by tallying the fossils with the photos of fossils that
were already identified.

Importance of fossils

1. The study of fossils helps to propose and construct the process of
evolution of living organism.

2. The study of fossils also helps to give information about the coal and
petroleum mines.

3. The study of fossils helps to discover geological history by determining
the age of rocks,

Fossil fuels

The fuels formed when the plants and animals get buried under the ground for
a long time, in presence of heat and pressure and in the absence of oxygen are
called fossil fuels. Coal, petroleum and natural gas are the most important
fossil fuels.

a. Coal

Coal is a fossil fuel formed by very compressed plants buried under the
ground for a very long time. They are black in colour and are very good
source of heat. Pure coal such as anthracite, produces heat without
smoke.

Process of formation of coal

Coal is the remains of trees, ferns and other plants that lived millions of
years ago. They were buried under the soil by natural disasters such as
earthquakes and volcanic eruptions. As more and more soil deposited

255


over them, they were compressed. The temperature also rose as they sank
deeper and deeper. As the process continued, they were protected from
biodegradation and oxidation. This trapped carbon slowly converted into
coal under high pressure and temperature in the absence of oxygen.

Importance of coal
1. Coal is used as a solid fuel to produce electricity and heat.

2. It is used as fuel in railway transportation, industries, brick factories,
etc.

3. It is also used for the manufacture of organic compound like
benzene, phenol, etc.

Mineral Oil (Petroleum)

Mineral oil or Petroleum is a dark coloured viscous liquid having very
bad odour. They are found naturally in petroleum mines. About 90-95%
of petroleum contains hydrocarbon and rest is oxygen, nitrogen, sulphur,
etc. Mineral oils are actually the remains of phytoplanktons and
zooplanktons buried under the earth crust millions of years ago.

Formation of mineral oils

Mineral oils are formed by the remains of phytoplankton and
zooplankton that are buried under the ocean bed by natural disasters such
as earthquakes and volcanic eruption. The climatic and geo-
morphological conditions of ancient earth was not as stable as it is today.
Drastic change in climate, huge volcanic eruption and massive
earthquakes took place time and again during which micro-organisms of
ocean got buried under the earth crust where they were compressed under
high temperature and pressure in the absence of oxygen. They finally
formed mineral oil or petroleum after the million of years.

Mineral oil directly recovered from mines is crude. They are subjected to
fractional distillation to separate into different components such as
petroleum gas, petrol, kerosene, lubricating oil, diesel, wax, bituminous,
asphalt and tar.

Importance of mineral oil

Different components obtained by the fractional distillation of crude
petroleum oil have different uses. Some of them are given in the table
below.

Climate Change and
Atmosphere

Unit 22

You might have noticed our snow-capped mountains becoming naked day by
day. The temperature of the carth is also increasing at an alarming rate
Similarly, the harmful ultra-violet rays are entering the earth surface through
the atmosphere. What do you think about the sole cause of all these changes
on earth? Suggest some ways to protect our planet earth from these hazards
for a safe life of all the creatures on earth.

Our earth consists of hydrosphere, lithosphere, atmosphere and biosphere.
Due to the presence of all the life supporting factors including suitable
temperature of the Earth, life has become possible in the earth. About 71 % of
the earth crust is covered with water. Atmosphere consists of different gases
such as nitrogen, oxygen, carbon dioxide, water vapour, etc. Existence of
atmosphere is due to the earth’s gravitational force. Adequate availability of
all these things has made the living beings to survive in the earth. Earth has
become the common home of all the living organisms. Due to growing
demand of the human beings, natural environment is being degraded day by
day.

Over population growth, industrialization, urbanization, etc. are the major
causes of environmental degradation. Increased number of vehicles,
establishment of industries, factories and chimneys, etc. are emitting harmful
chemicals and gases in the large amount. Over crowed human settlement,
improper disposal of wastes, use of excessive pesticides and insecticides and
chemical fertilizers cause adverse effect on the earth’s climate. As a result,
earth’s climate is rapidly changing.

Climate change refers to the change of global or regional climate over a long
period of time. It may be due to human activities or due to the natural causes.
Duc to this many negative consequences like global warming, disturbance on
the growth of organisms, less crop production, melting of snow of the
Himalayas, etc have been occurred. These consequences of the climate
change are really hazardous to the human beings and other organisms. The
major effect of climate change is increasing rate of diseases and mortality due
to droughts, floods, spreading of diseases like hepatitis, cholera, malaria ete. It
causes change in temperature, less production of crops, fruits and vegetables.
Global warming is another great result of climate change. Many rivers and
stream will dry up soon due to rapid melting of snow of the Himalayas. There

260


will be the scarcity of drinking water, water for irrigation and hydropower
production. There will be the difficulty for many organisms to adapt in the
changing environment.

Hence to reduce the impacts of climate change there should be the efforts
from every sector in an integrated way. Many efforts have been implemented
in the national and international level to reduce the impacts of climate change.
In this chapter, we will discuss the national and international efforts to
minimize the impacts of climate change, layers of atmosphere, ozone layer
depletion and industrial gases.

National and international efforts to minimize the effects of climate
change

Climate change is the great problem of today's world. It has been alarming in
context of global warming. The adverse effects of global warming have
mostly been noticed in developing countries like Nepal. It has caused heavy
rainfall, floods, landslides, draught and soil erosion. It has been seen that
altogether 14 glacier lakes outburst had happened in between 1935 and 1991
in Nepal. Climate change has caused many negative consequences on all the
living beings. So it’s the present need of every country to make necessary
efforts to minimize the impacts of climate change, United Nations
organization has started implementing various programs to reduce the effects
of climate change. Some efforts made in National and international level to
minimize the adverse effects of climate change are given below:

National efforts

a. National Communication Report

b. Climate Change Policy, 2067

¢. Climate Change Adaption Strategic Program
d. National Adaptation Program

e. Local Adaptation Program

f. Others programs

a. National Communication Report

  

‘Nepal has submitted the initial national communication report to the COP
(Conference of the Parties) of UNO protocol. In this report, Nepal has
mentioned the impacts of climate change, adaptational ways to the
change and various polices and laws to be implemented to combat
climate change. It has also focused on the necessity to research the
impact of climate change in various sectors like transportation, health,

261


c

communication, education, industries, agriculture, management of
wastes, etc.

Climate Change Policy, 2067

Global warming is the result of climate change. It adversely affects
human health, agriculture, forest and various human related aspects. In
this regard, the climate change policy has been formulated to create
awareness among the people and develop adaption.

Climate Change Adaptation Strategic Programme

Nepal was invited by climate investment fund, in the year 2009 to
participate in the global model programme related to adaptation to the
climate change. The world climate model program provides financial
support to the poor countries. The climate change adaptation program of
Nepal has been divided into five sectors : i) climate change adaptation of
watersheds of hilly regions ii) adaptation to risks induced by climate
change iii) develop capable community for climate change adaptation by
the initiation of local sectors iv) promotion of endangered species for
climate change adaptation v) main stream flow of the risk management of
climate change in development projects.

National Adaptation Program

‘National adaptation program was prepared in the year 2010 by the
Government of Nepal. It mainly evaluates the risk of climate change. It
has launched altogether 250 programmes integrating into 9 different
sectors.

Local Adaptation Program

Local adaptation program is specially designed for implementing in the
local level. It prepares and co-ordinates local and National level
programs. It conducts programs to minimize the impacts of climate
change at the local level to provide necessary services to the endangered
communities and region and family. It includes four theories progressive,
inclusive, capability and flexibility while selecting the process of climate
adaptation.

Other programs

Other programs includes programs related to improved chimneys of brick
factories, improved stove, use of biogas, pre-information system about
natural disasters etc.

The United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change
(UNFCCC)

UNFCCC was held in the year 1992 in Rio de Jenerio. There were 154
countries participated in the programme. This conference addressed
various aspects like increasing environmental pollution, sustainable
development programme etc. Climate change cannot be stopped
completely. So our life style should adapt to the changing environment.

UN Climate Change Conference

The UN conference on climate change has been conducted 19 times till
2013 AD to inform the works and programmes conducted in a country to
other member countries related to climate change. Nepal also has
prepared and implemented climate change policy-2011 on the basis of
UNFCCC 1992.

Agenda 21

This action plan was formulated on the basis of a slogan “think globally
and act locally” to conserve environment and ensure sustainable
development.

Intergovernmental Forum

Intergovernmental forum was established in the year 1988 A.D. It
prepares report to support the UNFCCC. It consists of the scientific,
technical and socio-economical information to understand the risk of
human caused due to climate change, adverse effects of climate change
and the mitigating measures.

263


5. Kyoto Protocol

It was adopted in December 1997 A.D. Its main objective is to reduce
climate change and production of greenhouse gases to control global
warming. The protocol makes 36 developed countries of the world to
reduce the emission of GHG by 5.25% by 2012 AD from their industries
The provision is now extended for 2020AD by the convention held in
2012 AD at Doha

6. Measures to reduce Greenhouse gases on the basis of Kyoto protocol

The Kyoto protocol encourages developed and developing countries to
work under the three market level mechanisms to meet their GHG
emission target. They are international emission trading, joint
implementation and clean development mechanisms.

7. Reduction of emission due to deforestation

Forests are the important natural resources for the absorption of carbon.
So, developed countries which produce large amount of greenhouse
gases should reduce the activities that destroy forest. Instead, the
developed countries should help underdeveloped countries to conserve
forest providing necessary support.

Atmosphere

The earth is surrounded by the atmosphere. Atmosphere is the layer of
different gases like nitrogen, oxygen, carbon dioxide etc. It is divided into five
different layers. They are troposphere, stratosphere, _mesosphere,
thermosphere and exosphere. The main gases are nitrogen 78%, oxygen 21%,
Argon 0.9%, carbon dioxide 0.03% and rest other gases like water vapour,
argon, other inert gases etc.

Troposphere

Troposphere is the lowermost layer of the atmosphere. It extends from 8-10
km at the poles and up to 16km at the equatorial region. So, it is extended up
to 16 km from the earth surface. It contains oxygen, Nitrogen, Carbon
dioxide, water vapour and dust particles. It is believed that about 95% of the
total mass of the atmosphere is present in this layer. The uppermost layer of
troposphere is called tropopause. Temperature of this layer decreases by 6.5°
C per km with rise of altitude from the earth’s surface. This layer is highly
affected by human activities. Troposphere is also called changeable layer
because temperature, humidity speed and direction of wind are continuously
going on changing within this layer.

264


Stratosphere

Stratosphere extends from 16km to 50km above the troposphere. It consists of
gases like Nitrogen, Oxygen, Ozone etc. it has a layer of ozone. The ozone
layer absorbs most of the harmful UV rays of the sun. So, this ozone layer
protects all the living beings from harmful rays. The upper boundary of this
layer is stratopause. The temperature increases with increase in altitude in this
region.

Mesosphere

Mesosphere extends from 50km to 80km above the stratosphere. It is the
coldest layer. The temperature decreases with the increase in altitude. It is the
coldest layer with the temperature about -109°C. Strong wind blows from
west to east in winter but east to west in rainy season.

Thermosphere

Thermosphere extends from 80 to 720km above the mesosphere. The density
of this layer is very low. It has great effect of solar radiation, So, temperature
increases with the rise of altitude, It contains the ions of various gases like
Nitrogen and oxygen. So, it is also called ionosphere

Exosphere

Exosphere is the outermost layer and extends above 720km from the earth’s
surface. It has low density of air. The temperature of this layer is above
1500°C. This layer is also called the fringe layer. It has low effect of earth’s
gravitation. So, the air molecules freely move towards the space.

Ozone layer

Ozone layer is present in the stratosphere. It consists of three atoms of
oxygen, When the ultraviolet rays breakdown the oxygen molecules, nascent
oxygen is formed which combines with normal oxygen molecule to form
ozone.

QO) ws 0+0

Q..0 ——+ 0;

Ozone layer extends from 25km to 40km from the earth surface. It absorbs
about 99% of ultraviolet rays and prevents them from entering into earth
surface. . It protects us from the diseases like blindness, skin cancer ete.
caused due to harmful rays. It helps to maintain suitable temperature of the
earth. It also preserves the ecosystem in the earth, Hence, it acts as a
protective layer for all of us and is called a protective layer.

265


Ozone formation also takes in the troposphere above the height of 12 km but
the amount of ozone in the troposphere is very low.

Depletion of Ozone layer

Depletion of ozone layer means the formation of hole in it or gradual thinning
of this layer. Depletion of ozone layer is caused due to the entry of chemicals
like chlorofluorocarbons, methyl chloroform, carbontetrachloride etc. into the
atmosphere. Chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs) are the major chemicals that deplete
the ozone layer. CFCs were discovered by T. Midgley in 1928 A.D. These
are the non toxic, non inflammable and cheap chemicals used as refrigerant.
When CFCs are reached into the atmosphere they deplete the ozone layer. UV
rays dissociate CFCs and form nascent chlorine. The nascent chlorine reacts
with ozone layer and gradually destroys this layer. The ozone hole was
observed above the Antarctica in 1885 A.D. for the first time.

Effects of depletion of ozone layer

1. Due to the depletion of ozone layer, harmful ultraviolet rays reach to the
earth. These rays may cause eye cataract, skin burning, skin cancer, etc to
the human beings. These rays may reduce the immunity power of body
and disturb the reproductive functions of the animals.

2, The ultraviolet rays are really the hindrance factors for the growth of
plants. They disturb the photosynthesis process and also reduce crop
production.

3. Depletion of ozone layer leads to the entrance of more solar radiations
into the earth surface which results global warming

266


4, Ultraviolet rays are changed into heat rays (infrared rays) after interacting
with the substances on earth causing global warming.

5. Depletion of ozone layer affects the components of an ecosystem. As a
result balanced ecosystem cannot be maintained.

Ways to protects ozone layer

i. Since chlorofluorocarbons are the main chemical that depletes ozone
layer, their use should be avoided.

ii, Alternatives sources of energy like solar energy, bio gas and
hydroelectricity should be used.

iii, We must reduce the excessive use of nitrogen fertilizers.
iv. We should encourage the use of hydro fluorocarbons instead of CFCs.
Industrial Gases

The various harmful gases like carbon dioxide, carbon monoxide, Sulphur
dioxide, nitrogen oxide etc. which are produced by the industries are called
industrial gases. Industries also release dust particles, smoke and solid wastes.
All these things pollute the atmosphere. The pollution caused due to such
gases and wastes is called industrial pollution.

When these gases reach to the atmosphere and react with rain water, they
form respective acids. It is given below;

Effects of industrial gases

 

1. When the gases like SO, SO3, NO? etc. react with rain water, they
forms acids. The acids rain corrodes monuments, buildings, temples,
bridges etc.

2. Industrial gases cause dizziness, headache, eye problem, chest pain, lung
cancer, bronchitis, asthma etc. to the human beings.

3. Carbon monoxide causes disturbance in the oxygen transport mechanism
of blood circulation.

4. Oxides of nitrogen also deplete the ozone layer as,

Accumulation of large amount of carbon dioxide in the atmosphere

Summary

lL.

Climate change refers to the change of global or regional climate
over a long period of time.

The major effect of climate change is increasing rate of diseases
and mortality.

Different national efforts made to minimize the effects of climate
change are, National Communication Report, Climate Change
Policy (2067); National Adaption Programme ete.

Different international efforts made to minimize the effects of climate
change are Agenda 21, Kyoto Protocol and minimizing the production of
green house gases.

The thick layer of gases around the earth is called atmosphere.
Atmosphere consists five layers. They are troposphere, stratosphere,
mesosphere, thermosphere and exosphere.

A layer of ozone is found in the stratosphere. So it is called Ozonosphere.

Ozonosphere prevents the entrance of harmful UV radiations into the
earth surface, so this layer is also called a protection layer.

Ozone layer is mainly destroyed by chlorofluorocarbons. Others
chemicals are methyl chloroform, carbon tetrachloride, methyl
bromide, nitrogen dioxide etc.

Depletion of ozone layer causes entrance of UV rays into the earth. It

results the greater impact on human health and it also disturbs the growth
of plants, crop production and affect other aquatic and terrestrial life.

. The gases that are release from the industries like CO2, CO, SO2, NO2

etc. are called industrial gases.

unit23 The Earth in the Universe

The vast and unlimited space containing all the mass and energy that exist is
called universe. The universe includes everything that exist, the most distant
stars, planets, satellites, as well as our earth and all the objects on it. Nobody
knows how big the universe is or whether it has any limits. The sun which
sustains all the life on our planet is only one of the billions and billions of
stars that exist in the universe, whereas the planet earth on which we live is
only a tiny speck in this vast space universe. The earth is one of the eight
planets, all of which revolve around a central star called sun. The billions of
star which exist in the universe are not distributed uniformly in space. These
star occurs in the form of clusters (or groups) of billions of stars called
galaxies.

 

In this chapter, we study in details about solar system, planets, satellites,
meters, comets, etc.

Solar system

The celestial bodies including planets, satellites, comets, etc. which revolve
around the sun form the solar system. It consists of eight planets, their
satellites (or moons), thousands of small heavenly bodies like meteors,
meteorites, plasma, asteroids, comets, charged particles and dust particles
The every members
of the solar family

The Sun

The Sun is a medium-sized star found at the center of solar system. It has the
largest members of solar family, The mass of sun is around 770 times greater
than the sum of masses of every other members of solar family. The sun
produces huge amount of heat energy due to the nuclear reactions occurred in
its core. It is the main sources of energy for solar system. It emits different
useful as well as harmful rays such as visible light ray, infra-red, ultraviolet,
x-ray, radio waves, etc. in the form of solar energy. But the harmful rays are
absorbed before they reach on the earth’s surface and does not cause any
sever harm.

Sun also blows solar wind of charged particles all around at very high speed
(500km/s) carrying adequate amount of heat and electro static energy.

The sun consists of abundant amount of hydrogen gases. The nuclear reaction
which converts the hydrogen nuclei into Helium nuclei in its core is
responsible for the production of large amount of solar energy.

Planets

Planets are named after "wanderer"as they keep on moving and their position
among the stars in sky keeps on changing every day. The massive heavenly
body that rounds the sun in an elliptical orbit is called planet. Planets do not
produce light, but reflect the light of their parents star. In our solar system,
there are eight planets, They are: Mercury, Venus, Earth, Mars, Jupiter,
Saturn, Uranus and Neptune. On the basis of their position, the planets are
divided two different groups. They are: inner planets and outer planets.

Those planets which lie inside the asteroid belt i.e. Mercury, Venus, Earth and
Mars are inner planets. These planets are also known as terrestrial planets.
Those planets which lie outside the asteroid belt i.e. Jupiter, Saturn, Uranus
and Neptune are outer planets.

The rocky particle lies in the space between the orbit of mars and Jupiter is
called asteroid belt. All planets except Mercury and Venus con
satellites. The heavenly body that revolves around a planet is

  

 

Planets revolve the sun. They receive heat and light from sun. They have their
own velocity, duration to complete a revolution and rotation, different number
of satellites, surface temperature, atmosphere etc. A short description about
each of the eight planets is given below.

Mercury (Budha)

It is the smallest, nearest and the fastest revolving planet from sun. It is
hardly seen by naked eyes from earth. It can only be seen at the horizon
just before sunrise or after sunset. It does not consist any satellites and
atmosphere. It is 5.8 x 10’ Km far from sun and 9.15 x 10’ Km far from
earth, Its diameter is 4851 Km. It is too hot at day (427° C) and too cold
at night (-170° C). Its rotation period is 59 days and revolution period is
88 days of earth. On observing it through earth, it seems like different
phases of moon.

Venus (Sukra)

It is the brightest, hottest and closest planet to the earth. It is also known
as twin planet of earth as it has approximately same size and mass. In the
early morning, it is visible in the eastern sky and visible in the western
sky in the evening, so termed as “morning and evening star”. It is 1.07
10° km far from the sun and approximately 4.2x 10’ km far from the
earth, Its diameter is 12035 km. Its rotation period is 243 days and
revolution period is 225 days. It doesn’t consist any satellites. It has
atmosphere of dense CO2, water vapor and clouds of H2SOy. This thick
atmosphere traps the solar radiation and the temperature rises to as high
as 480°C.

Earth is the only planet known where life exists. It is the third planet on
the basis of distance from the sun and fifth largest planet in the solar
system. The average surface temperature of the earth is 15° C. Earth
consists of 71% of water and 29% of land. It is 1.5 x 10°km far from sun
(1 AU). Its rotation period is 24hrs and revolution period is 365days 6hrs
(reasons for leap year). It consist of one natural satellite called moon. Its
atmosphere consists of Nz (78%), O (21%), CO2, HzO vapour, methane
etc.

Mars (Mangal)

Mars is the planet which is fourth in position from the sun. Due to the
presence of limonite (iron ore), it is red in color. So, called red planet and
can be seen easily from the earth. Its diameter is 6,742 km which is
approximately half the diameter of earth. It is about 2.3 x 10°km far from
sun and 7.8 x 10’ km far from earth. Its temperature during the day varies
like that of the earth but during the night it may fall below -38° C. Its
rotation period is 24hr 37 min and revolution period is 687 days. It

Jupiter (Brihaspati)

Jupiter is the largest planet of the solar system. It is around 319 times
bigger than the earth. Its average surface temperature is -143°C. Its
rotation period is 10 hr and revolution period is about 12 years. It is a
planet with maximum number of satellites i.e. 67. Its atmosphere consists
of Hz and He. It is always surrounded by dense clouds of methane and
ammonia so its surface is not seen clearly. It has a red spot in its
atmosphere which is assumed to be formed due to atmospheric hurricane.

Saturn (Sani)

Saturn is the second largest planet after Jupiter, It is surrounded by three
elliptical rings separated by dark gaps. The ring consists of many
individual pieces of mixture of ice and dust particles that travel around
the planet. This planet is second fastest than Jupiter for rotating about its
own axis. Its rotation period is 10 hr 30 min and revolution period is
29.5yrs. Its axis subtends an angle of 27° against its orbital plane. So, the
days and night are not equal at all places. It consists of 62 satellites
except particles in ring. Titan is the largest of them having 5,140 km
diameter. It is 1.5 x 10” km far from sun and 1.27 x 10° km far from the
earth. Its surface average temperature is -180° C and its atmosphere
consists of Hy and He.

Uranus (Arun)

Uranus was the planet discovered first. It is a giant ball of gas and liquid.
Its atmosphere consists of blue green clouds of methane, helium and
hydrogen. As like other planets, it is not solid. It is believed that water
lies beneath the level of ammonia and a rocky core is present in its
centre. It is 2.87x 10° km far from the sun and 2.73x 10° km far from the
earth. Its diameter is 50442 km and average surface temperature is -
216°C. Its rotation period is 17 hours 8 minutes and revolution period is
84 years. It consists of 27 satellites.

viii) Neptune (Barun)

Neptune is the farthest planet from the sun. Its surface consists of Hz, He,
Ne, silicate and water but its surface is not hard as the earth. This planet

274


contains a stony core and remaining most of the part is composed of
liquid and gases. This planet has a great dark spot as large as the earth is
seen. It is 4.48x10°km far from sun and 4.36x10° km from the earth. Its
surface average temperature is -220°C. Its rotation period is 16 hours and
revolution period is 164 years. It consists of 14 satellites. Triton is the
largest satellite among them having diameter approximately 2705 km.

[Note: Initially, Pluto was considered as a planet. But, it is removed from

of orbit of other planets]

Comets

The gaseous mass that revolves around the sun in highly elliptical path is
comet. It is made up of frozen gas, dust and ice. It is the tail or broom shaped
member of the solar system. They do not have their own light. They revolve
around the sun and have a very long period of revolution. A typical comets
consists of three main parts; the nucleus, the coma and the tail. The nucleus
consists of crumbly rock particles trapped inside a frozen matters. Along with
the dust particles, the evaporating layers form a hazy cloud called the coma.
Coma is surrounded by clouds of hydrogen gas.

The comets sometimes come very closer to the sun and moves far away from
the sun for the most time. When it comes closer to the sun, the ice and
gaseous particles get evaporated. The evaporated parts moved in opposite
direction to the sun due to solar wind, so it seems like a tail.

Meteors and meteorites

‘A meteor is a bright streak of light seen for a short duration in the sky on a
clear night. So, it is also called shooting star or falling star because it looks
like a star falling from one direction to the other in the sky. Very big and
bright meteor is also called fire ball

When a small celestial body falls rolling into gravitational field of the earth, it
is rapidly attracted towards the earth . Then there is friction between the body
and the atmosphere. The body gets heated due to the heat produced during
friction and then it starts glowing brightly and changes into gas and vapour.
As a result, it disappears on the way. It is called meteor shower. Some
meteors are little larger and do not burn completely as they travel through the
atmosphere and reach the surface of the planets or moon due to gravity. These
are called meteorites.

On the basic of nature of particles present in the meteorites, they are mainly of
three different types. They are stony, irony and stony iron. Those meteorites
which consists of more amount of slica and less amount of iron is stony
meteorites. Those meteorites which consists of more amount of iron and less
amount of silica is irony meteorites. While, those meteoroids which consist of
equal amount of silica and iron is stony iron meteorites. The meteorites land
on the surface of earth with high velocity and thus make fissures or holes
called craters. Normally, meteorites found on earth are of irony in nature.
They are of 100 gm to 20,000 kg. Meteorites help scientists to conduct many
investigations and studies on the nature of materials from which the solar
system was formed and many more.

 

About 50,000 years ago, a meteorite fell in Arizona of USA and a deep crater
was formed which is shown in alongside figure. The diameter of crater was
1265m and 175m deep. This can be seen nowadays too.

276


 

Fig.23.3 (a) Meteor Fig. 23.3 (b) Meteorite

The largest meteorite was fallen on the earth in 1920 AD in Namibia. It is
named as Hoba which is 60 metric tons. It is believed that about 250 million
visible meteors enter the earth’s atmosphere every day with the velocities
35km/s to 95km/s. About 500 meteorites hit the surface of the earth in a year.

 

Constellation

Constellations are groups of some stars, which do not change their location
relative to each other and always form a fixed pattern, There are 88
constellations known and out of them 12 constellations are used as a sign of
zodiac. The ancient human societies gave names to the constellations seen
from northern hemisphere resembling their shapes to the Greece god ,
animals, equipments etc. For example, Ursa major and Ursa minor, orion, Leo
and lion etc. Similarly, in the period of 1400 to 1700 AD, the researcher gave
names to the constellations seen towards southern hemisphere whose shape
like animals. For example, telescopiam , muska (from moth) etc.The position
of the pole star (Dhurba Tara) can be located with the help of Ursa major. All
constellations appear to revolve around the pole star which remains stationary.
This is because it is directly above North pole on the axis of rotation of the
earth.

Some superstitions regarding to zodiacs

Many people in world have some beliefs regarding the relation of their fate
with their own zodiac. Also in Hinduism it is determined by the position of
moon in sky against certain zodiac and its certain region (Nakshatra) during
their birth time. As the earth revolves around the sun, the sun traces a certain
path through the sky known as ecliptic. This path has 13 groups of stars,
among which 12 are considered by astrology as zodiac constellations. Zodiacs
are 12 out of 13 groups of constellations that have astrological significance.
These zodiac constellations are:

a. Aries g) Libra
b. Taurus h) Scorpius (Scorpio in astrology)

c. Gemini i) Sagittarius

Modern science has not proved any such relation between fate and their birth

279


There are millions of people in the world but constellations are only 88,
therefore there is no any scientific reason to determine the fate and future
of individuals with their own zodiac which is itself a common zodiac for
hundreds of thousands of people at the same time.

* Ifa groom has been born on new moon day, he is often called ‘Aunsia’ in
many rural communities, and bride for him is also chosen to be ‘Aunsia’
among many other alternatives, Otherwise, they think the life of those
couple wouldn’t go smoothly. It also has no scientific reason behind.

© It is believed in many society that the attitude of a person will be
accordingly the nature of their zodiac, but attitude is related with genetics
to some extent and mainly upon his/her environment during childhood,
schooling, profession of their parents, and the type of food they take, etc.

© Many of us select particular day for travelling and initiating some
important tasks not on the basis of their leisure, condition of weather,
economical situation and socio-political situation of the nation but on the
position of moon on certain zodiac and certain region around the bright
star (nakshatra) of the zodiac. It is also superstition.

* Many people prefer certain gems to put on accordingly as their zoidiac or
astrologist prescription, but there is no scientific reason behind it.

© In most of the arrange marriage, tallying of bride and groom’s zodiac in
practice and in many cases ignoring other important socio- economic and
educational, genetic aspects.

These are only some examples that resemble how deeply we have anchored
such unscientific norms and values. It is difficult and time consuming task to
make the society free of such superstition. Educating people is the only way
to get rid of it.

Importance of zodiacs

Familiar people can easily guess time and direction they want to know by
observing the position of zodiacs and other constellations in the sky. If
scattered stars of sky weren’t groups in different constellations, it would be
very difficult and mysterious to recognize them. Position of known stars and
constellation can be used to know observer’s actual position over water, air,
deserts and lonely places. Navigators, pilots, travelers, meteorologists use to
observe zodiacs and constellation regularly.

Galaxy

There are billions of stars in this universe but are not distributed uniformly in
space. These stars occur in huge bunches or clusters, each cluster contain
billions of stars. Such a big cluster of star is called a galaxy. Thus a galaxy is a
vast collection of billions of stars, hydrogen gas and dust clouds (nebulae)
isolated in space from similar systems. A typical large galaxy is 100000 light
years in diameter and contains hundred billion stars. There are about 100 billion
galaxies in the universe. So the total number of stars in the universe is 10” stars.

 

 

Astronomers have discovered at least one billion galaxies in the known part of
the universe. Two galaxies, the large Magellanic cloud and small Magellanic
cloud, are the closest neighbours to the earth’s galaxy, which is the milky way
galaxy. The one more important galaxy in the universe is Andromeda galaxy

Irregular galaxies tend to be smaller and fainter

might have been caused by gigantic explosions
at their centres. Thus, the stars forming an
irregular galaxy are unevenly distributed in the galaxy.

nearly spherical to flattened disks. These
galaxies are called elliptical galaxies.
They are very bright in the centre and do
not have spiral arms. Elliptical galaxies
contain very little dust and gas and are
generally older than the other types of galaxies.

Satellites

Satellites are the heavenly bodies that revolve around the planet in their own
orbit. The speed of a satellite around the planet is called orbital velocity which
depends directly to the mass of the planet and inversely to the distance from
the planet. As like the planets, they don’t have their own light. They reflect
the light rays coming from sun. There are 153 natural satellites in number.

Satellites are of two different types- Natural satellites and artificial satellites.

Those satellites which are found naturally revolving around the planet are
natural satellites, whereas man-made satellites kept at a geo-stationary orbit of
the space that revolve around the planets are artificial satellites. The moon is
the only natural satellite of the Earth. The mean distance between the earth
and the moon is 384,400 km. Moon’s surface area is 3.79*10’ km’. It has a
diameter of about 3476 km. The moon takes about 27.33 days to complete a
revolution around the earth which is called sidereal month. However, the time
from one full moon to the next is about 29.5 days which is called synodic
month.

All the planets except Mercury and Venus have natural satellites. There are
altogether 173 satellites of planets. The following table presents the number
of satellites of different planets:

Artificial satellite

The man made objects revolving round the
earth are called artificial satellites. The
artificial satellites are kept at a geo
stationary orbit at a height of 36,900 km
from the earth’s surface. They are sent with
the help of rockets to revolve round the
earth continuously. Solar cells are used in
artificial satellites to get energy. These are
controlled from the earth. The purposes of
launching artificial satellites are mentioned

 

below: AG, 28:12

a. To collect more and reliable information about solar system, stars,
nebulas and galaxies.

b. To conduct various scientific experiments which can’t be done on the
earth

c. To forecast weather.

d. To investigate different military and spying operations of enemies.

e. To research the life in outer space.

f. To establish space-laboratory and to make spaceship in future.

Summary

1. Solar system includes the sun and the heavenly bodies like planets,
satellites, comets, asteroids, meteoroids and interstellar dust and gases.
Most of them revolve round the sun.

2. The largest and heaviest mass of the solar system is the sun itself. Its
mass is approximately 1.99x10* kg.

3. Mercury, Venus, Earth and mars are inner planets whereas Jupiter,
Saturn, Uranus and Neptune are outer planets. The asteroid belt between
the orbits of Mars and Jupiter separates inner and outer planets.

4, Inner planets are called terrestrial planets as they have solid crust, Outer
planets lack solid crust; they are just gas-giants.

5. Small heavenly bodies made of dust and frozen gases that revolve round

the sun in the highly elliptical orbits are called comets. They appear as

283


“stars with tail” or a broom when approach to sun. A typical comet has
three parts: nucleus, coma and tail.

Sometimes in the clear night sky we see streak of light travelling with
very high speed in any direction for a very short period of time. They are
meteors, often called ‘falling stars’ or ‘shooting stars”

Small group of stars having fixed patterns resembling ancient gods,
goddess, animals or any scientific equipments are called constellations.
Till now, 88 such constellations are identified and given name by
astronomists.

Collection of millions of stars at a very vast region in space is called
galaxy. Galaxies are thousands of light years in dimensions and it is
believed that there are 10'? galaxies in the universe.

On the basis of shape, galaxies are categorized into spiral, elliptical and
irregular types.

10. Our solar system is situated at a distance of 30,000 light years from the

centre of Milky Way galaxy. It is a spiral type of galaxy having a disc
like shape with almost eight spiral arms radiating from the centre. This
galaxy has interstellar dust and gas particles in between the gap of two
stars. There are about 10" stars in this galaxy.

. Heavenly bodies that revolve round the planets are called satellites.
Satellites are categorized as natural and artificial. There are altogether
174 natural satellites in the solar system.

12. Artificial satellites are launched for various scientific purposes.
